<ol class="wpProQuiz_list">
									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10124,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28989}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>1</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>1</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="165">A company has a web application that uses Internet Information Services (IIS) for Windows Server. A file share is used to store the application data on the network-attached storage of the company’s on-premises data center. To achieve a highly available system, they plan to migrate the application and file share to AWS.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="487">Which of the following can be used to fulfill this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10124" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10124" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Migrate the existing file share configuration to AWS Storage Gateway.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10124" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon FSx for Windows File Server.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10124" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon EFS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10124" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon EBS.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon FSx for Windows File Server</strong> provides fully managed Microsoft Windows file servers, backed by a fully native Windows file system. Amazon FSx for Windows File Server has the features, performance, and compatibility to easily lift and shift enterprise applications to the AWS Cloud. It is accessible from Windows, Linux, and macOS compute instances and devices. Thousands of compute instances and devices can access a file system concurrently.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/FSx_Windows_File_Server_How-it-Works.9396055e727c3903de991e7f3052ec295c86f274.png" alt="Amazon FSx for Windows File Server | Cloud File Storage | Amazon Web Services" width="541" height="213" data-noaft="1"></p>
<p>In this scenario, you need to migrate your existing file share configuration to the cloud. Among the options given, the best possible answer is Amazon FSx. A file share is a specific folder in your file system, including the folder’s subfolders, which you make accessible to your compute instances via the SMB protocol. To migrate file share configurations from your on-premises file system, you must migrate your files first to Amazon FSx before migrating your file share configuration.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon FSx for Windows File Server</strong></span>.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Migrate&nbsp;the existing file share configuration to AWS Storage Gateway</strong></span> is incorrect because AWS Storage Gateway is primarily used to integrate your on-premises network to AWS but not for migrating your applications. Using a file share in Storage Gateway implies that you will still keep your on-premises systems, and not entirely migrate it.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon EFS</strong></span> is incorrect because it is stated in the scenario that the company is using a file share that runs on a Windows server. Remember that Amazon EFS only supports Linux workloads.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Migrate the existing file share configuration to Amazon EBS</strong></span> is incorrect because EBS is primarily used as block storage for EC2 instances and not as a shared file system. A file share is a specific folder in a file system that you can access using a server message block (SMB) protocol. Amazon EBS does not support SMB protocol.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/windows/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/windows/faqs/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/fsx/latest/WindowsGuide/migrate-file-share-config-to-fsx.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/fsx/latest/WindowsGuide/migrate-file-share-config-to-fsx.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Check out this Amazon FSx Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-fsx/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-fsx/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="multiple" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;multiple&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10082,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28925}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>2</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>2</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="168"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company plans to host a web application in an Auto Scaling group of Amazon EC2 instances. The application will be used globally by users to upload and store several types of files. Based on user trends, files that are older than 2 years must be stored in a different storage class. The Solutions Architect of the company needs to create a cost-effective and scalable solution to store the old files yet still provide durability and high availability.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="622"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Which of the following approach can be used to fulfill this requirement? (Select TWO.)</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10082" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10082" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon EFS and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon EFS-IA after 2 years.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10082" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon EBS volumes to store the files. Configure the Amazon Data Lifecycle Manager (DLM) to schedule snapshots of the volumes after 2 years.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10082" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon S3 and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon S3 Glacier after 2 years.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10082" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon S3 and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon S3 Standard-IA after 2 years. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10082" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use a RAID 0 storage configuration that stripes multiple Amazon EBS volumes together to store the files. Configure the Amazon Data Lifecycle Manager (DLM) to schedule snapshots of the volumes after 2 years.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon S3</strong> stores data as objects within buckets. An object is a file and any optional metadata that describes the file. To store a file in Amazon S3, you upload it to a bucket. When you upload a file as an object, you can set permissions on the object and any metadata. Buckets are containers for objects. You can have one or more buckets. You can control access for each bucket, deciding who can create, delete, and list objects in it. You can also choose the geographical region where Amazon S3 will store the bucket and its contents and view access logs for the bucket and its objects.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/lifecycle-transitions-v2.png" alt="Transitioning objects using Amazon S3 Lifecycle - Amazon Simple Storage Service" width="500" height="314"></p>
<p>To move a file to a different storage class, you can use Amazon S3 or Amazon EFS. Both services have lifecycle configurations. Take note that Amazon EFS can only transition a file to the IA storage class after 90 days. Since you need to move the files that are older than 2 years to a more cost-effective and scalable solution, you should use the Amazon S3 lifecycle configuration. With S3 lifecycle rules, you can transition files to S3 Standard IA or S3 Glacier. Using S3 Glacier expedited retrieval, you can quickly access your files within 1-5 minutes.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answers are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #008000;">– Use Amazon S3 and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon S3 Glacier after 2 years.</span></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #008000;">– Use Amazon S3 and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon S3 Standard-IA after 2 years.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Use Amazon EFS and create a lifecycle policy that will move the objects to Amazon EFS-IA after 2 years </strong></span>is incorrect because the maximum days for the EFS lifecycle policy is only 90 days. The requirement is to move the files that are older than 2 years or 730 days.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>&nbsp;Use Amazon EBS volumes to store the files. Configure the Amazon Data Lifecycle Manager (DLM) to schedule snapshots of the volumes after 2 years</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because Amazon EBS costs more and is not as scalable as Amazon S3. It has some limitations when accessed by multiple EC2 instances. There are also huge costs involved in using the multi-attach feature on a Provisioned IOPS EBS volume to allow multiple EC2 instances to access the volume.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>&nbsp;Use a RAID 0 storage configuration that stripes multiple Amazon EBS volumes together to store the files. Configure the Amazon Data Lifecycle Manager (DLM) to schedule snapshots of the volumes after 2 years</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because RAID (Redundant Array of Independent Disks) is just a data storage virtualization technology that combines multiple storage devices to achieve higher performance or data durability.&nbsp;RAID 0 can stripe multiple volumes together for greater I/O performance than you can achieve with a single volume. On the other hand, RAID 1 can mirror two volumes together to achieve on-instance redundancy.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/efs/latest/ug/lifecycle-management-efs.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/efs/latest/ug/lifecycle-management-efs.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/s3/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/s3/faqs/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

</p>
								</div>
							</div>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>3</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>3</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A telecommunications company is planning to give AWS Console access to developers. Company policy mandates the use of identity federation and role-based access control. Currently, the roles are already assigned using groups in the corporate Active Directory.</p>
<p>In this scenario, what combination of the following services can provide developers access to the AWS console? (Select TWO.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10126" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10126" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> IAM Groups												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10126" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> AWS Directory Service Simple AD												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10126" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> AWS Directory Service AD Connector												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10126" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Lambda												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10126" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> IAM Roles												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Considering that the company is using a corporate Active Directory, it is best to use&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>AWS Directory Service AD Connector</strong></span> for easier integration. In addition, since the roles are already assigned using groups in the corporate Active Directory, it would be better to&nbsp;also use <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>IAM Roles</strong></span>. Take note that you can assign an IAM Role to the users or groups from your Active Directory once it is integrated with your VPC via the AWS Directory Service AD Connector.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/directory_service_howitworks.80bfccbf2f5d1d63558ec3c086aff247147258f1.png" alt="" width="650" height="207"></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>AWS Directory Service</strong> provides multiple ways to use Amazon Cloud Directory and Microsoft Active Directory (AD) with other AWS services. Directories store information about users, groups, and devices, and administrators use them to manage access to information and resources. AWS Directory Service provides multiple directory choices for customers who want to use existing Microsoft AD or Lightweight Directory Access Protocol (LDAP)–aware applications in the cloud. It also offers those same choices to developers who need a directory to manage users, groups, devices, and access.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>AWS Directory Service Simple AD</strong></span> is incorrect because this just provides a <strong>subset</strong> of the features offered by AWS Managed Microsoft AD, including the ability to manage user accounts and group memberships, create and apply group policies, securely connect to Amazon EC2 instances, and provide Kerberos-based single sign-on (SSO). In this scenario, the more suitable component to use is the AD Connector since it is a directory gateway with which you can redirect directory requests to your on-premises Microsoft Active Directory.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>IAM Groups</strong></span> is incorrect because this&nbsp;is just a collection of&nbsp;<em>IAM</em>&nbsp;users.&nbsp;<em>Groups</em>&nbsp;let you specify permissions for multiple users, which can make it easier to manage the permissions for those users. In this scenario, the more suitable one to use is IAM Roles in order for permissions to create AWS Directory Service resources.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Lambda</strong></span> is incorrect because this is primarily used for serverless computing.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/how-to-connect-your-on-premises-active-directory-to-aws-using-ad-connector/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/how-to-connect-your-on-premises-active-directory-to-aws-using-ad-connector/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10085,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28940}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>4</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>4</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="204"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A content management system (CMS) is hosted on a fleet of auto-scaled, On-Demand EC2 instances that use Amazon Aurora as its database. Currently, the system stores the file documents that the users upload in one of the attached EBS Volumes. Your manager noticed that the system performance is quite slow and he has instructed you to improve the architecture of the system. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="579"><span data-renderer-mark="true">In this scenario, what will you do to implement a scalable, high-available POSIX-compliant shared file system?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10085" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10085" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an S3 bucket and use this as the storage for the CMS												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10085" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use EFS												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10085" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Upgrading your existing EBS volumes to Provisioned IOPS SSD Volumes												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10085" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use ElastiCache												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon Elastic File System (Amazon EFS)</strong> provides simple, scalable, elastic file storage for use with AWS Cloud services and on-premises resources. When mounted on Amazon EC2 instances, an Amazon EFS file system provides a standard file system interface and file system access semantics, allowing you to seamlessly integrate Amazon EFS with your existing applications and tools. Multiple Amazon EC2 instances can access an Amazon EFS file system at the same time, allowing Amazon EFS to provide a common data source for workloads and applications running on more than one Amazon EC2 instance.</p>
<p>This particular scenario tests your understanding of EBS, EFS, and S3. In this scenario, there is a fleet of On-Demand EC2 instances that store file documents from the users to one of the attached EBS Volumes. The system performance is quite slow because the architecture doesn’t provide the EC2 instances parallel shared access to the file documents.</p>
<p>Although an EBS Volume can be attached to multiple EC2 instances, you can only do so on instances within an availability zone. What we need is high-available storage that can span multiple availability zones. Take note as well that the type of storage needed here is “file storage” which means that <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>S3</strong></span> is not the best service to use because it is mainly used for “object storage”, and S3 does not provide the notion of “folders” too. This is why <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>using EFS</strong></span> is the correct answer.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-02-13_00-55-39-826ea8db5a1179c5f79d02b3b6cf1f2c.png" width="502" height="422"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Upgrading your existing EBS volumes to Provisioned IOPS SSD Volumes</strong></span> is incorrect because an EBS volume is a storage area network (SAN) storage and not a POSIX-compliant shared file system. You have to use EFS instead.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using ElastiCache</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;this is an in-memory data store that improves the performance of your applications, which is not what you need since it is not a file storage.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/efs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/efs/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Check out this Amazon EFS Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-efs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-efs/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Check out this Amazon S3 vs EBS vs EFS Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3-vs-ebs-vs-efs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3-vs-ebs-vs-efs/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10123,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28987}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>5</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>5</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A retail website has intermittent, sporadic, and unpredictable transactional workloads throughout the day that are hard to predict. The website is currently hosted on-premises and is slated to be migrated to AWS. A new relational database is needed that autoscales capacity to meet the needs of the application’s peak load and scales back down when the surge of activity is over.</p>
<p>Which of the following option is the MOST cost-effective and suitable database setup in this scenario?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10123" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10123" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Amazon Aurora Serverless DB cluster then set the minimum and maximum capacity for the cluster.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10123" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Amazon Aurora Provisioned DB cluster with burstable performance DB instance class types.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10123" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch a DynamoDB Global table with Auto Scaling enabled.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10123" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Amazon Redshift data warehouse cluster with Concurrency Scaling.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Amazon Aurora Serverless is an on-demand, auto-scaling configuration for Amazon Aurora. An&nbsp;Aurora Serverless DB cluster&nbsp;is a DB cluster that automatically starts up, shuts down, and scales up or down its compute capacity based on your application’s needs. Aurora Serverless provides a relatively simple, cost-effective option for infrequent, intermittent, sporadic or unpredictable workloads. It can provide this because it automatically starts up, scales compute capacity to match your application’s usage and shuts down when it’s not in use.</p>
<p>Take note that a non-Serverless DB cluster for Aurora is called a provisioned DB cluster. Aurora Serverless clusters and provisioned clusters both have the same kind of high-capacity, distributed, and highly available storage volume.</p>
<p>When you work with Amazon Aurora without Aurora Serverless (provisioned DB clusters), you can choose your DB instance class size and create Aurora Replicas to increase read throughput. If your workload changes, you can modify the DB instance class size and change the number of Aurora Replicas. This model works well when the database workload is predictable, because you can adjust capacity manually based on the expected workload.</p>
<p>However, in some environments, workloads can be intermittent and unpredictable. There can be periods of heavy workloads that might last only a few minutes or hours, and also long periods of light activity, or even no activity. Some examples are retail websites with intermittent sales events, reporting databases that produce reports when needed, development and testing environments, and new applications with uncertain requirements. In these cases and many others, it can be difficult to configure the correct capacity at the right times. It can also result in higher costs when you pay for capacity that isn’t used.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aurora-serverless-arch.png" alt="" width="550" height="468"></p>
<p>With Aurora Serverless , you can create a database endpoint without specifying the DB instance class size. You set the minimum and maximum capacity. With Aurora Serverless, the database endpoint connects to a<em>&nbsp;proxy fleet&nbsp;</em>that routes the workload to a fleet of resources that are automatically scaled. Because of the proxy fleet, connections are continuous as Aurora Serverless scales the resources automatically based on the minimum and maximum capacity specifications. Database client applications don’t need to change to use the proxy fleet. Aurora Serverless manages the connections automatically. Scaling is rapid because it uses a pool of “warm” resources that are always ready to service requests. Storage and processing are separate, so you can scale down to zero processing and pay only for storage.</p>
<p>Aurora Serverless introduces a new&nbsp;<code class="code">serverless</code>&nbsp;DB engine mode for Aurora DB clusters. Non-Serverless DB clusters use the&nbsp;<code class="code">provisioned</code>&nbsp;DB engine mode.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Launch an Amazon Aurora Serverless DB cluster then set the minimum and maximum capacity for the cluster.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launch an Amazon Aurora Provisioned DB cluster with burstable performance DB instance class types</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because an Aurora Provisioned DB cluster is not suitable for intermittent, sporadic, and unpredictable transactional workloads.&nbsp;This model works well when the database workload is predictable because you can adjust capacity manually based on the expected workload. A better database setup here is to use an Amazon Aurora Serverless cluster.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launch a DynamoDB Global table with Auto Scaling enabled</strong></span> is incorrect. Although it is using Auto Scaling, the scenario explicitly indicated that you need a relational database to handle your transactional workloads. DynamoDB is a NoSQL database and is not suitable for this use case. Moreover, the use of a DynamoDB Global table is not warranted since this is primarily used if you need a fully managed, multi-region, and multi-master database that provides fast, local, read and write performance for massively scaled, global applications.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launch an Amazon Redshift data warehouse cluster with Concurrency Scaling</strong>&nbsp;</span>is incorrect because this type of database is primarily used for online analytical processing (OLAP) and not for online transactional processing (OLTP). Concurrency Scaling&nbsp;is simply an Amazon Redshift feature that automatically and elastically scales query processing power of your Redshift cluster to provide consistently fast performance for hundreds of concurrent queries.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-serverless.how-it-works.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-serverless.how-it-works.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-serverless.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-serverless.html</a></p>
</p>
								</div>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>6</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>6</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A newly hired Solutions Architect is assigned to manage a set of CloudFormation templates that are used in the company’s cloud architecture in AWS. The Architect accessed the templates and tried to analyze the configured IAM policy for an S3 bucket.</p>
<pre>{ 
 "Version": "2012-10-17", 
 "Statement": [ 
  { 
   "Effect": "Allow", 
   "Action": [ 
    "s3:Get*", 
    "s3:List*" 
  ], 
  "Resource": "*" 
 }, 
 { 
   "Effect": "Allow", 
   "Action": "s3:PutObject", 
   "Resource": "arn:aws:s3:::boracay/*" 
  } 
 ] 
}
</pre>
<p>What does the above IAM policy allow? (Select THREE.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10659" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to write objects into the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects in the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket but not allowed to list the objects in the bucket.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects from all S3 buckets owned by the account.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to change access rights for the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="5">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="6" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read and delete objects from the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">6. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10659" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects from the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span>												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>You manage access in AWS by creating policies and attaching them to IAM identities (users, groups of users, or roles) or AWS resources. A policy is an object in AWS that, when associated with an identity or resource, defines their permissions. AWS evaluates these policies when an IAM principal (user or role) makes a request. Permissions in the policies determine whether the request is allowed or denied. Most policies are stored in AWS as JSON documents. AWS supports six types of policies: identity-based policies, resource-based policies, permissions boundaries, AWS Organizations SCPs, ACLs, and session policies.</p>
<p>IAM policies define permissions for action regardless of the method that you use to perform the operation. For example, if a policy allows the&nbsp;<a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/APIReference/API_GetUser.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">GetUser</a>&nbsp;action, then a user with that policy can get user information from the AWS Management Console, the AWS CLI, or the AWS API. When you create an IAM user, you can choose to allow console or programmatic access. If console access is allowed, the IAM user can sign in to the console using a user name and password. Or if programmatic access is allowed, the user can use access keys to work with the CLI or API.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/CC_Diagram1_0717.png" width="466" height="442"></p>
<p>Based on the provided IAM policy, the user is only allowed to get, write, and list all of the objects for the <code>boracay</code> s3 bucket. The <code>s3:PutObject</code> basically means that you can submit a PUT object request to the S3 bucket to store data.</p>
<p>Hence,&nbsp;the correct answers are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #008000;">– An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects from all S3 buckets owned by the account.</span></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #008000;">– An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to write objects into the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #008000;">– An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects from the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to change access rights for the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because the template does not have any statements which allow the user to change access rights in the bucket.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read objects in the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket but not allowed to list the objects in the bucket</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because it can clearly be seen in the template that there is a <code>s3:List*</code> which permits the user to list objects.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>An IAM user with this IAM policy is allowed to read and delete objects from the <code>boracay</code> S3 bucket</strong></span> is incorrect. Although you can read objects from the bucket, you cannot delete any objects.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/API/RESTObjectOps.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/API/RESTObjectOps.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/access_policies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/access_policies.html</a></p>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10125,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28991}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>7</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>7</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="177">A company collects atmospheric data such as temperature, air pressure, and humidity from different countries. Each site location is equipped with various weather instruments and a high-speed Internet connection. The average collected data in each location is around 500 GB and will be analyzed by a weather forecasting application hosted in Northern Virginia. As the Solutions Architect, you need to aggregate all the data in the fastest way.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="621">Which of the following options can satisfy the given requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10125" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10125" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Snowball Edge to transfer large amounts of data.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10125" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Upload the data to the closest S3 bucket. Set up a cross-region replication and copy the objects to the destination bucket.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10125" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a Site-to-Site VPN connection.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10125" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Transfer Acceleration in the destination bucket and upload the collected data using Multipart Upload.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon S3</strong> is object storage built to store and retrieve any amount of data from anywhere on the Internet. It’s a simple storage service that offers industry-leading durability, availability, performance, security, and virtually unlimited scalability at very low costs. Amazon S3 is also designed to be highly flexible. Store any type and amount of data that you want; read the same piece of data a million times or only for emergency disaster recovery; build a simple FTP application or a sophisticated web application.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/s3_ta_speed_compare_2.png" width="597" height="969"></p>
<p>Since the weather forecasting application is located in N.Virginia, you need to transfer all the data in the same AWS Region. With Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration, you can speed up content transfers to and from Amazon S3 by as much as 50-500% for long-distance transfer of larger objects. Multipart upload allows you to upload a single object as a set of parts. After all the parts of your object are uploaded, Amazon S3 then presents the data as a single object. This approach is the fastest way to aggregate all the data.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Enable Transfer Acceleration in the destination bucket and upload the collected data using Multipart Upload.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Upload the data to the closest S3 bucket. Set up a cross-region replication and copy the objects to the destination bucket</strong></span> is incorrect because replicating the objects to the destination bucket takes about 15 minutes. Take note that the requirement in the scenario is to aggregate the data in the fastest way.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Snowball Edge to transfer large amounts of data </strong></span>is incorrect because the end-to-end time to transfer up to 80 TB of data into AWS Snowball Edge is approximately one week.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a Site-to-Site VPN connection</strong></span> is incorrect because setting up a VPN connection is not needed in this scenario. Site-to-Site VPN is just used for establishing secure connections between an on-premises network and Amazon VPC. Also, this approach is not the fastest way to transfer your data. You must use Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/replication.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/replication.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/transfer-acceleration.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/transfer-acceleration.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10654,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28895}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>8</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>8</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An online medical system hosted in AWS stores sensitive Personally Identifiable Information (PII) of the users in an Amazon S3 bucket. Both the master keys and the unencrypted data should never be sent to AWS to comply with the strict compliance and regulatory requirements of the company.</p>
<p>Which S3 encryption technique should the Architect use?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10654" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10654" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use S3 server-side encryption with a KMS managed key.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10654" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use S3 client-side encryption with a KMS-managed customer master key. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10654" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use S3 client-side encryption with a client-side master key.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10654" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use S3 server-side encryption with customer provided key.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Client-side encryption</strong>&nbsp;is the act of encrypting data before sending it to Amazon S3. To enable client-side encryption, you have the following options:</p>
<p>– Use an AWS KMS-managed customer master key.</p>
<p>– Use a client-side master key.</p>
<p>When using an AWS KMS-managed customer master key to enable client-side data encryption, you provide an AWS KMS customer master key ID (CMK ID) to AWS. On the other hand, when you use client-side master key for client-side data encryption, <span style="text-decoration: underline;">your client-side master keys and your unencrypted data are never sent to AWS</span>. It’s important that you safely manage your encryption keys because if you lose them, you can’t decrypt your data.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/s3_sse_customer_key_2.png" alt="" width="700" height="179"></p>
<p>This is how client-side encryption using client-side master key works:</p>
<p><strong>When uploading an object</strong> – You provide a client-side master key to the Amazon S3 encryption client. The client uses the master key only to encrypt the data encryption key that it generates randomly. The process works like this:</p>
<p>1. The Amazon S3 encryption client generates a one-time-use symmetric key (also known as a data encryption key or data key) locally. It uses the data key to encrypt the data of a single Amazon S3 object. The client generates a separate data key for each object.</p>
<p>2. The client encrypts the data encryption key using the master key that you provide. The client uploads the encrypted data key and its material description as part of the object metadata. The client uses the material description to determine which client-side master key to use for decryption.</p>
<p>3. The client uploads the encrypted data to Amazon S3 and saves the encrypted data key as object metadata (<code>x-amz-meta-x-amz-key</code>) in Amazon S3.</p>
<p><strong>When downloading an object –&nbsp;</strong>The client downloads the encrypted object from Amazon S3. Using the material description from the object’s metadata, the client determines which master key to use to decrypt the data key. The client uses that master key to decrypt the data key and then uses the data key to decrypt the object.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is to <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>use S3 client-side encryption with a client-side master key</strong></span>.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using S3 client-side encryption with a KMS-managed customer master key</strong></span> is incorrect because in client-side encryption with a KMS-managed customer master key, you provide an AWS KMS customer master key ID (CMK ID) to AWS. The scenario clearly indicates that both the master keys and the unencrypted data should never be sent to AWS.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using S3 server-side encryption with a KMS managed key</strong></span> is incorrect because the scenario mentioned that the unencrypted data should never be sent to AWS, which means that you have to use client-side encryption in order to encrypt the data first before sending to AWS. In this way, you can ensure that there is no unencrypted data being uploaded to AWS. In addition, the master key used by Server-Side Encryption with AWS KMS–Managed Keys (SSE-KMS) is uploaded and managed by AWS, which directly violates the requirement of not uploading the master key.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using S3 server-side encryption with customer provided key</strong></span> is incorrect because just as mentioned above, you have to use client-side encryption in this scenario instead of server-side encryption. For the S3 server-side encryption with customer-provided key (SSE-C), you actually provide the encryption key as part of your request to upload the object to S3. Using this key, Amazon S3 manages both the encryption (as it writes to disks) and decryption (when you access your objects).</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/UsingEncryption.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/UsingEncryption.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/UsingClientSideEncryption.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/UsingClientSideEncryption.html</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10660,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28915}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>9</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>9</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A pharmaceutical company has resources hosted on both their on-premises network and in AWS cloud. They want all of their Software Architects to access resources on both environments using their on-premises credentials, which is stored in Active Directory.</p>
<p>In this scenario, which of the following can be used to fulfill this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10660" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10660" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use IAM users												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10660" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon VPC												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10660" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up SAML 2.0-Based Federation by using a Web Identity Federation.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10660" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up SAML 2.0-Based Federation by using a Microsoft Active Directory Federation Service (AD FS). 												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Since the company is using Microsoft Active Directory which implements&nbsp;Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML), you can set up a&nbsp;SAML-Based Federation for API Access to your AWS cloud. In this way, you can easily connect to AWS using the login credentials of your on-premises network.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/saml-based-sso-to-console.diagram.png" alt="" width="650" height="375"></p>
<p>AWS supports identity federation with SAML 2.0, an open standard that many identity providers (IdPs) use. This feature enables federated single sign-on (SSO), so users can log into the AWS Management Console or call the AWS APIs without you having to create an IAM user for everyone in your organization. By using SAML, you can simplify the process of configuring federation with AWS, because you can use the IdP’s service instead of writing custom identity proxy code.</p>
<p>Before you can use SAML 2.0-based federation as described in the preceding scenario and diagram, you must configure your organization’s IdP and your AWS account to trust each other. The general process for configuring this trust is described in the following steps. Inside your organization, you must have an IdP that supports SAML 2.0, like Microsoft Active Directory Federation Service (AD FS, part of Windows Server), Shibboleth, or another compatible SAML 2.0 provider.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Set up SAML 2.0-Based Federation by using a Microsoft Active Directory Federation Service (AD FS).</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Setting up SAML 2.0-Based Federation by using a Web Identity Federation</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because this is primarily used to let users sign in via a well-known external identity provider (IdP), such as Login with Amazon, Facebook, Google. It does not utilize Active Directory.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using IAM users</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;the situation requires you to use the existing credentials stored in their Active Directory, and not user accounts that will be generated by IAM.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using Amazon VPC</strong></span> is incorrect because this only lets you provision a logically isolated section of the AWS Cloud where you can launch AWS resources in a virtual network that you define. This has nothing to do with user authentication or Active Directory.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_saml.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">http://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_saml.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-identity-and-access-management-iam/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-identity-and-access-management-iam/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:8120,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28929}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>10</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>10</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A Docker application, which is running on an Amazon ECS cluster behind a load balancer, is heavily using DynamoDB. You are instructed to improve the database performance by distributing the workload evenly and using the provisioned throughput efficiently.</p>
<p>Which of the following would you consider to implement for your DynamoDB table?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="8120" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_8120" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Avoid using a composite primary key, which is composed of a partition key and a sort key.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_8120" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use partition keys with low-cardinality attributes, which have a few number of distinct values for each item.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_8120" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use partition keys with high-cardinality attributes, which have a large number of distinct values for each item.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_8120" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Reduce the number of partition keys in the DynamoDB table.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>The partition key portion of a table’s primary key determines the logical partitions in which a table’s data is stored. This in turn affects the underlying physical partitions. Provisioned I/O capacity for the table is divided evenly among these physical partitions. Therefore a partition key design that doesn’t distribute I/O requests evenly can create “hot” partitions that result in throttling and use your provisioned I/O capacity inefficiently.</p>
<p>The optimal usage of a table’s provisioned throughput depends not only on the workload patterns of individual items, but also on the partition-key design. This doesn’t mean that you must access all partition key values to achieve an efficient throughput level, or even that the percentage of accessed partition key values must be high. It does mean that the more distinct partition key values that your workload accesses, the more those requests will be spread across the partitioned space. In general, you will use your provisioned throughput more efficiently as the ratio of partition key values accessed to the total number of partition key values increases.</p>
<p>One example for this is the use of <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>partition keys with high-cardinality attributes, which have a large number of distinct values for each item</strong></span>.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Reducing the number of partition keys in the DynamoDB table</strong></span> is incorrect. Instead of doing this, you should actually add more to improve its performance to distribute the I/O requests evenly and not avoid “hot” partitions.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using partition keys with low-cardinality attributes, which have a few number of distinct values for each item</strong></span> is incorrect because this is the exact opposite of the correct answer. Remember that the more distinct partition key values your workload accesses, the more those requests will be spread across the partitioned space. Conversely, the less distinct partition key values, the less evenly spread it would be across the partitioned space, which effectively slows the performance.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Avoid using a composite primary key, which is composed of a partition key and a sort key</strong></span> is incorrect because as mentioned, a composite primary key will provide more partition for the table and in turn, improves the performance. Hence, it should be used and not avoided.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-partition-key-uniform-load.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-partition-key-uniform-load.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/database/choosing-the-right-dynamodb-partition-key/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"> https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/database/choosing-the-right-dynamodb-partition-key/</a></p>
