									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10640,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28927}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>11</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>11</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A Solutions Architect needs to make sure that the On-Demand EC2 instance can only be accessed from this IP address (110.238.98.71) via an SSH connection. Which configuration below will satisfy this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10640" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10640" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Security Group Inbound Rule: Protocol – TCP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/32												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10640" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Security Group Inbound Rule: Protocol – UDP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/0												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10640" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Security Group Inbound Rule: Protocol – UDP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/32												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10640" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Security Group Inbound Rule: Protocol – TCP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/0												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>A <strong>security group</strong> acts as a virtual firewall for your instance to control inbound and outbound traffic. When you launch an instance in a VPC, you can assign up to five security groups to the instance. Security groups act at the instance level, not the subnet level. Therefore, each instance in a subnet in your VPC can be assigned to a different set of security groups.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/AWS-SG-InboundRuleSSH.PNG" width="700" height="239"></p>
<p>The requirement is to only allow the individual IP of the client and not the entire network. Therefore, the proper CIDR notation should be used. The /32 denotes one IP address and the /0 refers to the entire network. Take note that the SSH protocol uses TCP and port 22.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Protocol – TCP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/32</strong></span></p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Protocol – UDP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/32</span></strong> and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Protocol – UDP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/0</strong></span> are incorrect as they are using UDP.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Protocol – TCP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/0</strong></span> is incorrect because it uses a /0 CIDR notation.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Protocol – TCP, Port Range – 22, Source 110.238.98.71/0</strong></span> is incorrect because it allows the entire network instead of a single IP.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/using-network-security.html#security-group-rules" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/using-network-security.html#security-group-rules</a></p>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10602,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28911}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>12</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>12</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Applications and Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="188">A payment processing company plans to migrate its on-premises application to an Amazon EC2 instance. An IPv6 CIDR block is attached to the company’s Amazon VPC. Strict security policy mandates that the production VPC must only allow outbound communication over IPv6 between the instance and the internet but should prevent the internet from initiating an inbound IPv6 connection. The new architecture should also allow traffic flow inspection and traffic filtering.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="655">What should a solutions architect do to meet these requirements?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10602" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10602" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach an Egress-Only Internet Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use AWS Network Firewall to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10602" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch the EC2 instance to a public subnet and attach an Internet Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use Traffic Mirroring to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10602" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach AWS PrivateLink interface endpoint to the VPC to control outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use Amazon GuardDuty to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10602" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach a NAT Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use AWS Firewall Manager to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>An <strong>egress-only internet gateway</strong> is a horizontally scaled, redundant, and highly available VPC component that allows outbound communication over IPv6 from instances in your VPC to the internet and prevents it from initiating an IPv6 connection with your instances.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/egress-only-igw.png" alt="" width="438" height="545"></p>
<p>IPv6 addresses are globally unique and are therefore public by default. If you want your instance to be able to access the internet, but you want to prevent resources on the internet from initiating communication with your instance, you can use an egress-only internet gateway.</p>
<p>A <strong>subnet</strong> is a range of IP addresses in your VPC. You can launch AWS resources into a specified subnet. Use a <strong>public subnet</strong> for resources that must be connected to the internet and a <strong>private subnet</strong> for resources that won’t be connected to the internet.</p>
<p>AWS Network Firewall is a managed service that makes it easy to deploy essential network protections for all of your Amazon Virtual Private Clouds (VPCs). The service can be set up with just a few clicks and scales automatically with your network traffic, so you don’t have to worry about deploying and managing any infrastructure. AWS Network Firewall includes features that provide protection from common network threats.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-network-firewall-filtering-inspection.png" alt="" width="1000" height="559"></p>
<p>AWS Network Firewall’s stateful firewall can incorporate context from traffic flows, like tracking connections and protocol identification, to enforce policies such as preventing your VPCs from accessing domains using an unauthorized protocol. AWS Network Firewall’s intrusion prevention system (IPS) provides active traffic flow inspection so you can identify and block vulnerability exploits using signature-based detection. AWS Network Firewall also offers web filtering that can stop traffic to known bad URLs and monitor fully qualified domain names.</p>
<p>In this scenario, you can use an egress-only internet gateway to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet and then use the AWS Network Firewall to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer for the scenario is: <strong><span style="color: #008000;">Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach an Egress-Only Internet Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use AWS Network Firewall to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach AWS PrivateLink interface endpoint to the VPC to control outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use Amazon GuardDuty to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering</strong></span>is incorrect because the AWS PrivateLink (which is also known as VPC Endpoint) is just a highly available, scalable technology that enables you to privately connect your VPC to the AWS services as if they were in your VPC. This service is not capable of controlling outbound IPv6 communication to the Internet. Furthermore, the Amazon GuardDuty service doesn’t have the features to do traffic inspection or filtering.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>&nbsp;Launch the EC2 instance to a public subnet and attach an Internet Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use Traffic Mirroring to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering</strong></span>is incorrect because an Internet Gateway does not limit or control any outgoing IPv6 connection. Take note that the requirement is to prevent the Internet from initiating an inbound IPv6 connection to your instance. This solution allows all kinds of traffic to initiate a connection to your EC2 instance hence, this option is wrong. In addition, the use of Traffic Mirroring is not appropriate as well. This is just an Amazon VPC feature that you can use to copy network traffic from an elastic network interface of type interface, not to filter or inspect the incoming/outgoing traffic.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong> <span style="color: #ff6600;">Launch the EC2 instance to a private subnet and attach a NAT Gateway to the VPC to allow outbound IPv6 communication to the internet. Use AWS Firewall Manager to set up the required rules for traffic inspection and traffic filtering</span></strong>is incorrect as because a NAT Gateway is only applicable for IPv4, not IPv6. You have to use the egress-only Internet Gateway instead. Moreover, the AWS Firewall Manager is neither capable of doing traffic inspection nor traffic filtering.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/egress-only-internet-gateway.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/egress-only-internet-gateway.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/configure-subnets.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/configure-subnets.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/VPC_Internet_Gateway.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/VPC_Internet_Gateway.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>13</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>13</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="191"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company conducted a surprise IT audit on all of the AWS resources being used in the production environment. During the audit activities, it was noted that you are using a combination of Standard and Convertible Reserved EC2 instances in your applications.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="450"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Which of the following are the characteristics and benefits of using these two types of Reserved EC2 instances? (Select TWO.)</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="9364" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_9364" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Unused Standard Reserved Instances can later be sold at the Reserved Instance Marketplace.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_9364" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> It runs in a VPC on hardware that's dedicated to a single customer.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_9364" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Convertible Reserved Instances allow you to exchange for another convertible reserved instance of a different instance family.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_9364" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> It can enable you to reserve capacity for your Amazon EC2 instances in multiple Availability Zones and multiple AWS Regions for any duration.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_9364" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Unused Convertible Reserved Instances can later be sold at the Reserved Instance Marketplace.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Reserved Instances (RIs)</strong> provide you with a significant discount (up to 75%) compared to On-Demand instance pricing. You have the flexibility to change families, OS types, and tenancies while benefiting from RI pricing when you use Convertible RIs. One important thing to remember here is that Reserved Instances are not physical instances, but rather a billing discount applied to the use of On-Demand Instances in your account.</p>
<p>The offering class of a Reserved Instance is either Standard or Convertible. A <strong>Standard Reserved Instance</strong> provides a more significant discount than a <strong>Convertible Reserved Instance</strong>, but you can’t exchange a Standard Reserved Instance unlike Convertible Reserved Instances. You can modify Standard and Convertible Reserved Instances. Take note that in Convertible Reserved Instances, you are allowed to exchange another Convertible Reserved instance with a different instance type and tenancy.</p>
<p>The configuration of a Reserved Instance comprises a single instance type, platform, scope, and tenancy over a term. If your computing needs change, you might be able to modify or exchange your Reserved Instance.</p>
<p>When your computing needs change, you can modify your Standard or Convertible Reserved Instances and continue to take advantage of the billing benefit. You can modify the Availability Zone, scope, network platform, or instance size (within the same instance type) of your Reserved Instance. You can also sell your unused instance for Standard RIs but not Convertible RIs on the Reserved Instance Marketplace.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct options are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Unused Standard Reserved Instances can later be sold at the Reserved Instance Marketplace.</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Convertible Reserved Instances allow you to exchange for another convertible reserved instance of a different instance family.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Unused Convertible Reserved Instances can later be sold at the Reserved Instance Marketplace</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect. This is not possible. Only Standard RIs can be sold at the Reserved Instance Marketplace.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>It can enable you to reserve capacity for your Amazon EC2 instances in multiple Availability Zones and multiple AWS Regions for any duration</strong></span> is incorrect because you can reserve capacity&nbsp;to a specific AWS Region (regional Reserved Instance) or specific Availability Zone (zonal Reserved Instance) only. You cannot reserve capacity to&nbsp;<span style="text-decoration: underline;">multiple</span> AWS Regions in a single RI purchase.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>It runs in a VPC on hardware that’s dedicated to a single customer</strong></span> is incorrect because that is the description of a Dedicated instance and not a Reserved Instance. A Dedicated instance runs in a VPC on hardware that’s dedicated to a single customer.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/reserved-instances/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/reserved-instances/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ec2-reserved-instances.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ec2-reserved-instances.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/reserved-instances-types.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/reserved-instances-types.html&nbsp;</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>14</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>14</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A Solutions Architect is hosting a website in an Amazon S3 bucket named <code>tutorialsdojo</code>. The users load the website using the following URL: <code>http://tutorialsdojo.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com</code> and there is a new requirement to add a JavaScript on the webpages in order to make authenticated HTTP <code>GET</code> requests against the same bucket by using the Amazon S3 API endpoint (<code>tutorialsdojo.s3.amazonaws.com</code>). Upon testing, you noticed that the web browser blocks JavaScript from allowing those requests.</p>
<p>Which of the following options is the MOST suitable solution that you should implement for this scenario?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10676" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10676" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Cross-Region Replication (CRR).												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10676" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Cross-Zone Load Balancing.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10676" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable cross-account access.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10676" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Cross-origin resource sharing (CORS) configuration in the bucket.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Cross-origin resource sharing (CORS) defines a way for client web applications that are loaded in one domain to interact with resources in a different domain. With CORS support, you can build rich client-side web applications with Amazon S3 and selectively allow cross-origin access to your Amazon S3 resources.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/cors-overview.png" alt="" width="754" height="362">Suppose that you are hosting a website in an Amazon S3 bucket named <code class="code">your-website</code>&nbsp;and your users load the website endpoint&nbsp;<code class="code">http://your-website.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com</code>. Now you want to use JavaScript on the webpages that are stored in this bucket to be able to make authenticated GET and PUT requests against the same bucket by using the Amazon S3 API endpoint for the bucket, <code class="code">your-website.s3.amazonaws.com</code>. A browser would normally block JavaScript from allowing those requests, but with CORS you can configure your bucket to explicitly enable cross-origin requests from&nbsp;<code class="code">your-website.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com</code>.</p>
<p>In this scenario, you can solve the issue by enabling the CORS in the S3 bucket. Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>enabling Cross-origin resource sharing (CORS) configuration in the bucket</strong></span> is the correct answer.</p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Enabling cross-account access</span></strong> is incorrect because cross-account access is a feature in IAM and not in Amazon S3.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enabling Cross-Zone Load Balancing</strong></span> is incorrect because Cross-Zone Load Balancing is only used in ELB and not in S3.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enabling Cross-Region Replication (CRR)</strong></span> is incorrect because CRR is a bucket-level configuration that enables automatic, asynchronous copying of objects across buckets in different AWS Regions.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/cors.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">http://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/cors.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ManageCorsUsing.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ManageCorsUsing.html</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10090,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28956}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>15</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>15</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="159">An organization needs a persistent block storage volume that will be used for mission-critical workloads. The backup data will be stored in an object storage service and after 30 days, the data will be stored in a data archiving storage service.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="407">What should you do to meet the above requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10090" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10090" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Attach an instance store volume in your existing EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 Glacier.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10090" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Attach an EBS volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10090" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Attach an EBS volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 Glacier.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10090" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Attach an instance store volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon Elastic Block Store (EBS)</strong> is an easy-to-use, high-performance block storage service designed for use with Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2) for both throughput and transaction-intensive workloads at any scale. A broad range of workloads, such as relational and non-relational databases, enterprise applications, containerized applications, big data analytics engines, file systems, and media workflows are widely deployed on Amazon EBS.</p>
<p><strong>Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3)</strong> is an object storage service that offers industry-leading scalability, data availability, security, and performance. This means customers of all sizes and industries can use it to store and protect any amount of data for a range of use cases, such as websites, mobile applications, backup and restore, archive, enterprise applications, IoT devices, and big data analytics.</p>
<p>In an <strong>S3 Lifecycle configuration</strong>, you can define rules to transition objects from one storage class to another to save on storage costs. Amazon S3 supports a waterfall model for transitioning between storage classes, as shown in the diagram below:</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/lifecycle-transitions-v2.png" alt=" Amazon S3 storage class waterfall graphic. " width="545" height="342"></p>
<p>In this scenario, three services are required to implement this solution. The mission-critical workloads mean that you need to have a persistent block storage volume and the designed service for this is Amazon EBS volumes. The second workload needs to have an object storage service, such as Amazon S3, to store your backup data. Amazon S3 enables you to configure the lifecycle policy from S3 Standard to different storage classes. For the last one, it needs archive storage such as Amazon S3 Glacier.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Attach an EBS volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 Glacier.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Attach an EBS volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA</strong></span> is incorrect because this lifecycle policy will transition your objects into an infrequently accessed storage class and not a storage class for data archiving.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Attach an instance store volume in your existing EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 Glacier</strong></span> is incorrect because an Instance Store volume is simply a temporary block-level storage for EC2 instances. Also, you can’t attach instance store volumes to an instance after you’ve launched it. You can specify the instance store volumes for your instance only when you launch it.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Attach an instance store volume in your EC2 instance. Use Amazon S3 to store your backup data and configure a lifecycle policy to transition your objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA</strong></span> is incorrect. Just like the previous option, the use of instance store volume is not suitable for mission-critical workloads because the data can be lost if the underlying disk drive fails, the instance stops, or if the instance is terminated. In addition, Amazon S3 Glacier is a more suitable option for data archival instead of Amazon S3 One Zone-IA.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/AmazonEBS.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/AmazonEBS.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/s3/storage-classes/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/s3/storage-classes/</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>16</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>16</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A suite of web applications is hosted in an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances across three Availability Zones and is configured with default settings. There is an Application Load Balancer that forwards the request to the respective target group on the URL path. The scale-in policy has been triggered due to the low number of incoming traffic to the application.</p>
<p>Which EC2 instance will be the first one to be terminated by your Auto Scaling group?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="7341" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7341" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The EC2 instance launched from the oldest launch configuration												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7341" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The instance will be randomly selected by the Auto Scaling group												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7341" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The EC2 instance which has been running for the longest time												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7341" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The EC2 instance which has the least number of user sessions												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>The default termination policy is designed to help ensure that your network architecture spans Availability Zones evenly. With the default termination policy, the behavior of the Auto Scaling group is as follows:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">1. If there are instances in multiple Availability Zones, choose the Availability Zone with the most instances and at least one instance that is not protected from scale in. If there is more than one Availability Zone with this number of instances, choose the Availability Zone with the instances that use the oldest launch configuration.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">2. Determine which unprotected instances in the selected Availability Zone use the oldest launch configuration. If there is one such instance, terminate it.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">3. If there are multiple instances to terminate based on the above criteria, determine which unprotected instances are closest to the next billing hour. (This helps you maximize the use of your EC2 instances and manage your Amazon EC2 usage costs.) If there is one such instance, terminate it.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">4. If there is more than one unprotected instance closest to the next billing hour, choose one of these instances at random.</p>
<p>The following flow diagram illustrates how the default termination policy works:</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/ASG-default-policy-evaluation-flowchart.png" width="460" height="900"></p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html#default-termination-policy" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html#default-termination-policy</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10684,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28899}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>17</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>17</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="224"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company is designing a banking portal that uses Amazon ElastiCache for Redis as its distributed session management component. Since the other Cloud Engineers in your department have access to your ElastiCache cluster, you have to secure the session data in the portal by requiring them to enter a password before they are granted permission to execute Redis commands. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="596"><span data-renderer-mark="true">As the Solutions Architect, which of the following should you do to meet the above requirement?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10684" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10684" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Authenticate the users using Redis AUTH by creating a new Redis Cluster with both the <code>--transit-encryption-enabled</code> and <code>--auth-token</code> parameters enabled.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10684" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up a Redis replication group and enable the <code>AtRestEncryptionEnabled</code> parameter.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10684" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an IAM Policy and MFA which requires the Cloud Engineers to enter their IAM credentials and token before they can access the ElastiCache cluster.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10684" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable the in-transit encryption for Redis replication groups.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Using <strong>Redis&nbsp;<code class="code">AUTH</code></strong>&nbsp;command can improve data security by requiring the user to enter a password before they are granted permission to execute Redis commands on a password-protected Redis server. Hence, the correct answer is:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Authenticate the users using Redis AUTH by creating a new Redis Cluster with both the <code>--transit-encryption-enabled</code> and <code>--auth-token</code> parameters enabled.</strong></span></p>
<p>To require that users enter a password on a password-protected Redis server, include the parameter&nbsp;<code class="code"><strong>--auth-token</strong></code>&nbsp;with the correct password when you create your replication group or cluster and on all subsequent commands to the replication group or cluster.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/ElastiCache-Redis-Secure-Compliant.png" alt="" width="600" height="381"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Setting up an IAM Policy and MFA which requires the Cloud Engineers to enter their IAM credentials and token before they can access the ElastiCache cluster</strong></span> is incorrect because this is not possible in IAM. You have to use the Redis AUTH option instead.</p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Setting up a Redis replication group and enabling the</span> <code>AtRestEncryptionEnabled</code> parameter</strong> is incorrect because&nbsp;the Redis At-Rest Encryption feature only secures&nbsp;the data inside&nbsp;the in-memory data store. You have to use Redis AUTH option instead.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enabling the in-transit encryption for Redis replication groups</strong></span> is incorrect. Although in-transit encryption is part of the solution, it is missing the most important thing which is the Redis AUTH option.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References</strong>:</p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/red-ug/auth.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/red-ug/auth.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/red-ug/encryption.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/red-ug/encryption.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10664,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28965}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>18</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>18</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A travel photo sharing website is using Amazon S3 to serve high-quality photos to visitors of your website. After a few days, you found out that there are other travel websites linking and using your photos. This resulted in financial losses for your business.</p>
<p>What is the MOST effective method to mitigate this issue?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10664" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10664" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use CloudFront distributions for your photos.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10664" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure your S3 bucket to remove public read access and use pre-signed URLs with expiry dates.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10664" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Block the IP addresses of the offending websites using NACL.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10664" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Store and privately serve the high-quality photos on Amazon WorkDocs instead.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>In Amazon S3, all objects are private by default. Only the object owner has permission to access these objects. However, the object owner can optionally share objects with others by creating a pre-signed URL, using their own security credentials, to grant time-limited permission to download the objects.</p>
<p>When you create a pre-signed URL for your object, you must provide your security credentials, specify a bucket name, an object key, specify the HTTP method (GET to download the object) and expiration date and time. The pre-signed URLs are valid only for the specified duration.</p>
<p>Anyone who receives the pre-signed URL can then access the object. For example, if you have a video in your bucket and both the bucket and the object are private, you can share the video with others by generating a pre-signed URL.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-02-13_00-58-48-19fb174d579477b46d422a9b264f6455.jpg" width="638" height="479"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using CloudFront distributions for your photos</strong></span> is incorrect. CloudFront is a content delivery network service that speeds up delivery of content to your customers.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Blocking the IP addresses of the offending websites using NACL</strong></span> is also incorrect. Blocking IP address using NACLs is not a very efficient method because a quick change in IP address would easily bypass this configuration.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Storing and privately serving the high-quality photos on Amazon WorkDocs instead</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect as WorkDocs is simply a fully managed, secure content creation, storage, and collaboration service. It is not a suitable service for storing static content. Amazon WorkDocs is more often used to easily create, edit, and share documents for collaboration and not for serving object data like Amazon S3.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ShareObjectPreSignedURL.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ShareObjectPreSignedURL.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ObjectOperations.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/ObjectOperations.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/s3-pre-signed-urls-vs-cloudfront-signed-urls-vs-origin-access-identity-oai/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/s3-pre-signed-urls-vs-cloudfront-signed-urls-vs-origin-access-identity-oai/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:6185,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28938}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>19</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>19</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="162">A company plans to migrate its on-premises workload to AWS. The current architecture is composed of a Microsoft SharePoint server that uses a Windows shared file storage. The Solutions Architect needs to use a cloud storage solution that is highly available and can be integrated with Active Directory for access control and authentication.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="504">Which of the following options can satisfy the given requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="6185" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_6185" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a file system using Amazon FSx for Windows File Server and join it to an Active Directory domain in AWS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_6185" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a Network File System (NFS) file share using AWS Storage Gateway.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_6185" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Amazon EC2 Windows Server to mount a new S3 bucket as a file volume.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_6185" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a file system using Amazon EFS and join it to an Active Directory domain.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon FSx for Windows File Server </strong>provides fully managed, highly reliable, and scalable file storage that is accessible over the industry-standard Service Message Block (SMB) protocol. It is built on Windows Server, delivering a wide range of administrative features such as user quotas, end-user file restore, and Microsoft Active Directory (AD) integration. Amazon FSx is accessible from Windows, Linux, and MacOS compute instances and devices. Thousands of compute instances and devices can access a file system concurrently.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/AWS-FSx-AD.PNG" width="700" height="222"></p>
<p>Amazon FSx works with Microsoft Active Directory to integrate with your existing Microsoft Windows environments. You have two options to provide user authentication and access control for your file system: AWS Managed Microsoft Active Directory and Self-managed Microsoft Active Directory.</p>
<p>Take note that after you create an Active Directory configuration for a file system, you can’t change that configuration. However, you can create a new file system from a backup and change the Active Directory integration configuration for that file system. These configurations allow the users in your domain to use their existing identity to access the Amazon FSx file system and to control access to individual files and folders.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:<span style="color: #008000;"><strong> Create a file system using Amazon FSx for Windows File Server and join it to an Active Directory domain in AWS.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create a file system using Amazon EFS and join it to an Active Directory domain </strong></span>is incorrect because Amazon EFS does not support Windows systems, only Linux OS. You should use Amazon FSx for Windows File Server instead to satisfy the requirement in the scenario.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>&nbsp;Launch an Amazon EC2 Windows Server to mount a new S3 bucket as a file volume</strong></span> is incorrect because you can’t integrate Amazon S3 with your existing Active Directory to provide authentication and access control.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create a Network File System (NFS) file share using AWS Storage Gateway </strong></span>is incorrect because NFS file share is mainly used for Linux systems. Remember that the requirement in the scenario is to use a Windows shared file storage. Therefore, you must use an SMB file share instead, which supports Windows OS and Active Directory configuration. Alternatively, you can also use the Amazon FSx for Windows File Server file system.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/fsx/latest/WindowsGuide/aws-ad-integration-fsxW.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/fsx/latest/WindowsGuide/aws-ad-integration-fsxW.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/windows/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/windows/faqs/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/userguide/CreatingAnSMBFileShare.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/userguide/CreatingAnSMBFileShare.html</a></p>

</p>
								</div>
							</div>
						
						
													<input type="button" name="skip" value="Skip question" class="wpProQuiz_button wpProQuiz_QuestionButton" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; display: none;">
												<input type="button" name="back" value="Back" class="wpProQuiz_button wpProQuiz_QuestionButton" style="float: left ; margin-right: 10px ; display: none;">
												<input type="button" name="check" value="Check" class="wpProQuiz_button wpProQuiz_QuestionButton" style="float: right; margin-right: 10px; display: none;">
												<input type="button" name="next" data-id="normal-next" value="Save &amp; Next" class="wpProQuiz_button wpProQuiz_QuestionButton" style="float: right; display: none;">

						<div style="clear: both;"></div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10089,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28952}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>20</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>20</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="190">A company has a cloud architecture that is composed of Linux and Windows EC2 instances that process high volumes of financial data 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. To ensure high availability of the systems, the Solutions Architect needs to create a solution that allows them to monitor the memory and disk utilization metrics of all the instances.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="539">Which of the following is the most suitable monitoring solution to implement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10089" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10089" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Install the CloudWatch agent to all the EC2 instances that gather the memory and disk utilization data. View the custom metrics in the Amazon CloudWatch console.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10089" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use the default CloudWatch configuration to EC2 instances where the memory and disk utilization metrics are already available. Install the AWS Systems Manager (SSM) Agent to all the EC2 instances.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10089" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable the Enhanced Monitoring option in EC2 and install CloudWatch agent to all the EC2 instances to be able to view the memory and disk utilization in the CloudWatch dashboard.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10089" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon Inspector and install the Inspector agent to all EC2 instances.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon CloudWatch</strong> has available Amazon EC2 Metrics for you to use for monitoring CPU utilization, Network utilization, Disk performance, and Disk Reads/Writes. In case you need to monitor the below items, you need to prepare a custom metric using a Perl or other shell script, as there are no ready to use metrics for:</p>
<ol>
<li>Memory utilization</li>
<li>Disk swap utilization</li>
<li>Disk space utilization</li>
<li>Page file utilization</li>
<li>Log collection</li>
</ol>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aeb-container-cw.png" width="650" height="397"></p>
<p>Take note that there is a multi-platform CloudWatch agent which can be installed on both Linux and Windows-based instances. You can use a single agent to collect both system metrics and log files from Amazon EC2 instances and on-premises servers. This agent supports both Windows Server and Linux and enables you to select the metrics to be collected, including sub-resource metrics such as per-CPU core. It is recommended that you use the new agent instead of the older monitoring scripts to collect metrics and logs.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <strong><span style="color: #008000;">Install the CloudWatch agent to all the EC2 instances that gathers the memory and disk utilization data. View the custom metrics in the Amazon CloudWatch console.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use the default CloudWatch configuration to EC2 instances where the memory and disk utilization metrics are already available. Install the AWS Systems Manager (SSM) Agent to all the EC2 instances</strong></span> is incorrect because, by default, CloudWatch does not automatically provide memory and disk utilization metrics of your instances. You have to set up custom CloudWatch metrics to monitor the memory, disk swap, disk space, and page file utilization of your instances.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enable the Enhanced Monitoring option in EC2 and install CloudWatch agent to all the EC2 instances to be able to view the memory and disk utilization in the CloudWatch dashboard</strong></span> is incorrect because Enhanced Monitoring is a feature of Amazon RDS. By default, Enhanced Monitoring metrics are stored for 30 days in the CloudWatch Logs.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use Amazon Inspector and install the Inspector agent to all EC2 instances</strong></span> is incorrect because Amazon Inspector is an automated security assessment service that helps you test the network accessibility of your Amazon EC2 instances and the security state of your applications running on the instances. It does not provide a custom metric to track the memory and disk utilization of each and every EC2 instance in your VPC.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/monitoring_ec2.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/monitoring_ec2.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/mon-scripts.html#using_put_script" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/mon-scripts.html#using_put_script</a></p>
