									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10703,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28997}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>21</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>21</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="173">A company requires all the data stored in the cloud to be encrypted at rest. To easily integrate this with other AWS services, they must have full control over the encryption of the created keys and also the ability to immediately remove the key material from AWS KMS. The solution should also be able to audit the key usage independently of AWS CloudTrail.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="532">Which of the following options will meet this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10703" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10703" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Key Management Service to create a CMK in a custom key store and store the non-extractable key material in Amazon S3.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10703" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Key Management Service to create AWS-owned CMKs and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10703" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Key Management Service to create a CMK in a custom key store and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10703" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Key Management Service to create AWS-managed CMKs and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>The <strong>AWS Key Management Service (KMS)</strong> custom key store feature combines the controls provided by <strong>AWS CloudHSM</strong> with the integration and ease of use of AWS KMS. You can configure your own CloudHSM cluster and authorize AWS KMS to use it as a dedicated key store for your keys rather than the default AWS KMS key store. When you create keys in AWS KMS you can choose to generate the key material in your CloudHSM cluster. CMKs that are generated in your custom key store never leave the HSMs in the CloudHSM cluster in plaintext and all AWS KMS operations that use those keys are only performed in your HSMs.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/KMS_01.png" alt="Figure 1: A cluster of two CloudHSM instances is connected to the KMS front-end hosts to create a customer controlled key store" width="527" height="244"></p>
<p>AWS KMS can help you integrate with other AWS services to encrypt the data that you store in these services and control access to the keys that decrypt it. To immediately remove the key material from AWS KMS, you can use a custom key store. Take note that each custom key store is associated with an AWS CloudHSM cluster in your AWS account. Therefore, when you create an AWS KMS CMK in a custom key store, AWS KMS generates and stores the non-extractable key material for the CMK in an AWS CloudHSM cluster that you own and manage. This is also suitable if you want to be able to audit the usage of all your keys independently of AWS KMS or AWS CloudTrail.</p>
<p>Since you control your AWS CloudHSM cluster, you have the option to manage the lifecycle of your CMKs independently of AWS KMS. There are four reasons why you might find a custom key store useful:</p>
<ol>
<li>You might have keys that are explicitly required to be protected in a single-tenant HSM or in an HSM over which you have direct control.</li>
<li>You might have keys that are required to be stored in an HSM that has been validated to FIPS 140-2 level 3 overall (the HSMs used in the standard AWS KMS key store are either validated or in the process of being validated to level 2 with level 3 in multiple categories).</li>
<li>You might need the ability to immediately remove key material from AWS KMS and to prove you have done so by independent means.</li>
<li>You might have a requirement to be able to audit all use of your keys independently of AWS KMS or AWS CloudTrail.</li>
</ol>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use AWS Key Management Service to create a CMK in a custom key store and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM</strong></span>.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Key Management Service to create a CMK in a custom key store and store the non-extractable key material in Amazon S3</strong></span> is incorrect because Amazon S3 is not a suitable storage service to use in storing encryption keys. You have to use AWS CloudHSM instead.</p>
<p>The options that say:&nbsp;<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Use AWS Key Management Service to create AWS-owned CMKs and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM </span></strong>and&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Key Management Service to create AWS-managed CMKs and store the non-extractable key material in AWS CloudHSM</strong></span> are both incorrect because the scenario requires you to have<span class="st"> full control over the encryption of the created key. AWS-owned CMKs and AWS-managed CMKs are managed by AWS. Moreover, these options do not allow you to audit the key usage independently of AWS CloudTrail.<br>
</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/kms/latest/developerguide/custom-key-store-overview.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/kms/latest/developerguide/custom-key-store-overview.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/kms/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/kms/faqs/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/are-kms-custom-key-stores-right-for-you/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/security/are-kms-custom-key-stores-right-for-you/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

</p>
								</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10118,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28969}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>22</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>22</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="195"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company is using a combination of API Gateway and Lambda for the web services of the online web portal that is being accessed by hundreds of thousands of clients each day. They will be announcing a new revolutionary product and it is expected that the web portal will receive a massive number of visitors all around the globe. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="526"><span data-renderer-mark="true">How can you protect the backend systems and applications from traffic spikes?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10118" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10118" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use throttling limits in API Gateway												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10118" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Deploy Multi-AZ in API Gateway with Read Replica												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10118" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> API Gateway will automatically scale and handle massive traffic spikes so you do not have to do anything.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10118" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Manually upgrade the EC2 instances being used by API Gateway												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon API Gateway</strong> provides throttling at multiple levels including global and by a service call. Throttling limits can be set for standard rates and bursts. For example, API owners can set a rate limit of 1,000 requests per second for a specific method in their REST APIs, and also configure Amazon API Gateway to handle a burst of 2,000 requests per second for a few seconds.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/New-API-GW-Diagram.c9fc9835d2a9aa00ef90d0ddc4c6402a2536de0d.png" width="700" height="308"></p>
<p>Amazon API Gateway tracks the number of requests per second. Any requests over the limit will receive a 429 HTTP response. The client SDKs generated by Amazon API Gateway retry calls automatically when met with this response.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use throttling limits in API Gateway.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>API Gateway will automatically scale and handle massive traffic spikes so you do not have to do anything</strong></span> is incorrect. Although it can scale using AWS Edge locations, you still need to configure the throttling to further manage the bursts of your APIs.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Manually upgrading the EC2 instances being used by API Gateway</strong></span> is incorrect because API Gateway is a fully managed service and hence, you do not have access to its underlying resources.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Deploying Multi-AZ in API Gateway with Read Replica</strong></span> is incorrect because RDS has Multi-AZ and Read Replica capabilities, and not API Gateway.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/faqs/#Throttling_and_Caching" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/faqs/#Throttling_and_Caching</a></p>

</p>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10142,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29021}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>23</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>23</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="165">A company plans to launch an Amazon EC2 instance in a private subnet for its internal corporate web portal. For security purposes, the EC2 instance must send data to Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon S3 via private endpoints that don’t pass through the public Internet.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="429">Which of the following can meet the above requirements?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10142" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10142" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Direct Connect to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10142" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Transit Gateway to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10142" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use VPC endpoints to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10142" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS VPN CloudHub to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>A <strong>VPC endpoint</strong> allows you to privately connect your VPC to supported AWS and VPC endpoint services powered by AWS PrivateLink without needing an Internet gateway, NAT computer, VPN connection, or AWS Direct Connect connection. Instances in your VPC do not require public IP addresses to communicate with resources in the service. Traffic between your VPC and the other service does not leave the Amazon network.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/ddb-yes-vpc-endpoint.png" alt=" Workflow diagram showing an EC2 instance accessing DynamoDB through a router and VPC endpoint only." width="557" height="307"></p>
<p>In the scenario, you are asked to configure private endpoints to send data to Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon S3 without&nbsp;accessing the public Internet.&nbsp;Among the options given, VPC endpoint is the most suitable service that will allow you to&nbsp;use private IP addresses to access both DynamoDB and S3 without any&nbsp;exposure to the public internet.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is the option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use VPC endpoints to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Use AWS Transit Gateway to route all access in S3 and DynamoDB to a public endpoint</span></strong>&nbsp;is incorrect because a Transit Gateway simply connects your VPC and on-premises networks through a central hub. It acts as a cloud router that allows you to integrate multiple networks.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Use AWS Direct Connect to route all access to S3 and DynamoDB via private endpoints</span>&nbsp;</strong>is&nbsp;incorrect because AWS Direct Connect is primarily used to establish a dedicated network connection from your premises to AWS. The scenario didn’t say that the company is using its on-premises server or has a hybrid cloud architecture.</p>
<p>The option that says: <strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Use AWS VPN CloudHub to route all access in S3 and DynamoDB to a private endpoint</span>&nbsp;</strong>is incorrect because&nbsp;AWS VPN CloudHub is mainly used&nbsp;to provide secure communication between remote sites and not for creating a private endpoint to access Amazon S3 and DynamoDB within the Amazon network.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/vpc-endpoints-dynamodb.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/vpc-endpoints-dynamodb.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/glue/latest/dg/vpc-endpoints-s3.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/glue/latest/dg/vpc-endpoints-s3.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-vpc/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-vpc/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10120,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28975}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>24</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>24</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>There are a lot of outages in the Availability Zone of your RDS database instance to the point that you have lost access to the database. What could you do to prevent losing access to your database in case that this event happens again?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10120" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10120" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a read replica												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10120" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Increase the database instance size												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10120" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Multi-AZ failover 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10120" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Make a snapshot of the database												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Amazon RDS Multi-AZ deployments provide enhanced availability and durability for Database (DB) Instances, making them a natural fit for production database workloads. For this scenario,&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>enabling Multi-AZ failover</strong></span> is the correct answer. When you provision a Multi-AZ DB Instance, Amazon RDS automatically creates a primary DB Instance and synchronously replicates the data to a standby instance in a different Availability Zone (AZ). Each AZ runs on its own physically distinct, independent infrastructure, and is engineered to be highly reliable.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/con-multi-AZ.png" alt="" width="484" height="344"></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>In case of an infrastructure failure, Amazon RDS performs an automatic failover to the standby (or to a read replica in the case of Amazon Aurora), so that you can resume database operations as soon as the failover is complete.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Making a snapshot of the database</strong></span> allows you to have a backup of your database, but it does not provide immediate availability in case of AZ failure. So this is incorrect.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Increasing the database instance size</strong></span> is not a solution for this problem. Doing this action addresses the need to upgrade your compute capacity but does not solve the requirement of providing access to your database even in the event of a loss of one of the Availability Zones.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Creating a read replica</strong></span> is incorrect because this simply provides enhanced performance for read-heavy database workloads. Although you can promote a read replica, its asynchronous replication might not provide you the latest version of your database.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Check out this Amazon RDS Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-relational-database-service-amazon-rds/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-relational-database-service-amazon-rds/</a></p>

</p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="multiple" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;multiple&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10140,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29010}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>25</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>25</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A global IT company with offices around the world has multiple AWS accounts. To improve efficiency and drive costs down, the Chief Information Officer (CIO) wants to set up a solution that centrally manages their AWS resources. This will allow them to procure AWS resources centrally and share resources such as AWS Transit Gateways, AWS License Manager configurations, or Amazon Route 53 Resolver rules across their various accounts.</p>
<p>As the Solutions Architect, which combination of options should you implement in this scenario? (Select TWO.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10140" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10140" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use the AWS Resource Access Manager (RAM) service to easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10140" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use the AWS Identity and Access Management service to set up cross-account access that will easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10140" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Control Tower to easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10140" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Consolidate all of the company's accounts using AWS Organizations.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10140" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Consolidate all of the company's accounts using AWS ParallelCluster.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>AWS Resource Access Manager (RAM) is a service that enables you to easily and securely share AWS resources with any AWS account or within your AWS Organization. You can share AWS Transit Gateways, Subnets, AWS License Manager configurations, and Amazon Route 53 Resolver rules resources with RAM.</p>
<p>Many organizations use multiple accounts to create administrative or billing isolation, and limit the impact of errors. RAM eliminates the need to create duplicate resources in multiple accounts, reducing the operational overhead of managing those resources in every single account you own. You can create resources centrally in a multi-account environment, and use RAM to share those resources across accounts in three simple steps: create a Resource Share, specify resources, and specify accounts. RAM is available to you at no additional charge.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/product-page-diagram_AWS-Resource-Access-Manager(1).379df75d48a8e2cc6160859b7ca3626a9b9be0c1.png" alt="" width="700" height="278"></p>
<p>You can procure AWS resources centrally, and use RAM to share resources such as subnets or License Manager configurations with other accounts. This eliminates the need to provision duplicate resources in every account in a multi-account environment, reducing the operational overhead of managing those resources in every account.</p>
<p>AWS Organizations is an account management service that lets you consolidate multiple AWS accounts into an organization that you create and centrally manage. With Organizations, you can create member accounts and invite existing accounts to join your organization. You can organize those accounts into groups and attach policy-based controls.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct combination of options in this scenario is:</p>
<p><strong>&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;">–&nbsp;Consolidate all of the company’s accounts using AWS Organizations.</span></strong></p>
<p><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>&nbsp;– Use the AWS Resource Access Manager (RAM) service to easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use the AWS Identity and Access Management service to set up cross-account access that will easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts</strong>&nbsp;</span>is incorrect. Although you can delegate access to resources that are in different AWS accounts using IAM, this process is extremely tedious and entails a lot of operational overhead since you have to manually set up cross-account access to each and every AWS account of the company. A better solution is to use AWS Resources Access Manager instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Control Tower to easily and securely share your resources with your AWS accounts&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect because AWS Control Tower simply offers the easiest way to set up and govern a new, secure, multi-account AWS environment. This is not the most suitable service to use to securely share your resources across AWS accounts or within your Organization. You have to use AWS Resources Access Manager (RAM) instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Consolidate all of the company’s accounts using AWS ParallelCluster </strong></span>is incorrect because&nbsp;AWS ParallelCluster is simply an AWS-supported open-source cluster management tool that makes it easy for you to deploy and manage High-Performance Computing (HPC) clusters on AWS. In this particular scenario, it is more appropriate to use AWS Organizations to consolidate all of your AWS accounts.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ram/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/ram/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ram/latest/userguide/shareable.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ram/latest/userguide/shareable.html</a></p>
</p>
								</div>
							</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10589,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28962}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>26</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>26</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A logistics company plans to automate its order management application. The company wants to use SFTP file transfer in uploading business-critical documents. Since the files are confidential, the files need to be highly available and must be encrypted at rest. The files must also be automatically deleted a month after they are created.</p>
<p>Which of the following options should be implemented to meet the company requirements with the least operation overhead?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10589" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10589" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Provision an Amazon EC2 instance and install the SFTP service. Mount an encrypted EFS file system on the EC2 instance to store the uploaded files. Add a cron job to delete the files older than a month.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10589" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Amazon Elastic Filesystem (EFS) file system and enable encryption. Configure AWS Transfer for SFTP to securely upload files to the EFS file system. Apply an EFS lifecycle policy to delete files after 30 days.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10589" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Amazon S3 bucket with encryption enabled. Configure AWS Transfer for SFTP to securely upload files to the S3 bucket. Configure the retention policy on the SFTP server to delete files after a month.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10589" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Amazon S3 bucket with encryption enabled. Launch an AWS Transfer for SFTP endpoint to securely upload files to the S3 bucket. Configure an S3 lifecycle rule to delete files after a month.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS Transfer for SFTP</strong> enables you to easily move your file transfer workloads that use the Secure Shell File Transfer Protocol (SFTP) to AWS without needing to modify your applications or manage any SFTP servers.</p>
<p>To get started with AWS Transfer for SFTP (AWS SFTP) you create an SFTP server and map your domain to the server endpoint, select authentication for your SFTP clients using service-managed identities, or integrate your own identity provider, and select your Amazon S3 buckets to store the transferred data. Your existing users can continue to operate with their existing SFTP clients or applications. Data uploaded or downloaded using SFTP is available in your Amazon S3 bucket, and can be used for archiving or processing in AWS.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/saa_aws_transfer_family.jpg"><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/saa_aws_transfer_family.jpg" alt="" width="700" height="238"></a></p>
<p>An <strong>Amazon S3 Lifecycle</strong> configuration is a set of rules that define actions that Amazon S3 applies to a group of objects. There are two types of actions:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Transition actions – These actions define when objects transition to another storage class. For example, you might choose to transition objects to the S3 Standard-IA storage class 30 days after creating them.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Expiration actions – These actions define when objects expire. Amazon S3 deletes expired objects on your behalf.</p>
<p>Therefore, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Create an Amazon S3 bucket with encryption enabled. Launch an AWS Transfer for SFTP endpoint to securely upload files to the S3 bucket. Configure an S3 lifecycle rule to delete files after a month. </strong></span>You can use S3 as the storage service for your AWS Transfer SFTP-enabled server.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an Amazon S3 bucket with encryption enabled. Configure AWS Transfer for SFTP to securely upload files to the S3 bucket. Configure the retention policy on the SFTP server to delete files after a month</strong></span> is incorrect. The 30-day retention policy must be configured on the Amazon S3 bucket. There is no retention policy option on AWS Transfer for SFTP.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an Amazon Elastic Filesystem (EFS) file system and enable encryption. Configure AWS Transfer for SFTP to securely upload files to the EFS file system. Apply an EFS lifecycle policy to delete files after 30 days</strong></span> is incorrect. This may be possible, however, the EFS lifecycle management doesn’t delete objects. It can only transition files in and out of the “Infrequent Access” tier.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Provision an Amazon EC2 instance and install the SFTP service. Mount an encrypted EFS file system on the EC2 instance to store the uploaded files. Add a cron job to delete the files older than a month</strong></span> is incorrect. This option is possible however, it entails greater operational overhead since you need to manage the EC2 instance and SFTP service.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/aws-transfer-family/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/aws-transfer-family/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/transfer/latest/userguide/create-server-sftp.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/transfer/latest/userguide/create-server-sftp.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10686,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28905}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>27</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>27</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="215"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A software development company is using serverless computing with AWS Lambda to build and run applications without having to set up or manage servers. They have a Lambda function that connects to a MongoDB Atlas, which is a popular Database as a Service (DBaaS) platform and also uses a third party API to fetch certain data for their application. One of the developers was instructed to create the environment variables for the MongoDB database hostname, username, and password as well as the API credentials that will be used by the Lambda function for DEV, SIT, UAT, and PROD environments. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="810"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Considering that the Lambda function is storing sensitive database and API credentials, how can this information be secured to prevent other developers in the team, or anyone, from seeing these credentials in plain text? Select the best option that provides maximum security.</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10686" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10686" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable SSL encryption that leverages on AWS CloudHSM to store and encrypt the sensitive information.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10686" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> There is no need to do anything because, by default, AWS Lambda already encrypts the environment variables using the AWS Key Management Service.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10686" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> AWS Lambda does not provide encryption for the environment variables. Deploy your code to an EC2 instance instead.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10686" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a new KMS key and use it to enable encryption helpers that leverage on AWS Key Management Service to store and encrypt the sensitive information.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>When you create or update Lambda functions that use environment variables, AWS Lambda encrypts them using the AWS Key Management Service. When your Lambda function is invoked, those values are decrypted and made available to the Lambda code.</p>
<p>The first time you create or update Lambda functions that use environment variables in a region, a default service key is created for you automatically within AWS KMS. This key is used to encrypt environment variables. However, if you wish to use encryption helpers and use KMS to encrypt environment variables after your Lambda function is created, you must create your own AWS KMS key and choose it instead of the default key. The default key will give errors when chosen. Creating your own key gives you more flexibility, including the ability to create, rotate, disable, and define access controls, and to audit the encryption keys used to protect your data.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-07-26_21-22-58-bc110e8ef8d91e32af6af839a0296911.png" alt="" width="700" height="319"></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">There is no need to do anything because, by default, AWS Lambda already encrypts the environment variables using the AWS Key Management Service</span></strong> is incorrect. Although Lambda encrypts the environment variables in your function by default, the sensitive information would still be visible to other users who have access to the Lambda console. This is because Lambda uses a default KMS key to encrypt the variables, which is usually accessible by other users. The best option in this scenario is to use encryption helpers to secure your environment variables.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enable SSL encryption that leverages on AWS CloudHSM to store and encrypt the sensitive information</strong></span> is also incorrect since enabling SSL would encrypt data only when in-transit. Your other teams would still be able to view the plaintext at-rest. Use AWS KMS instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>AWS Lambda does not provide encryption for the environment variables. Deploy your code to an EC2 instance instead</strong></span> is incorrect since, as mentioned, Lambda does provide encryption functionality of environment variables.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/env_variables.html#env_encrypt" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/env_variables.html#env_encrypt</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/tutorial-env_console.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/tutorial-env_console.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10646,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28999}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>28</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>28</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="182">A company hosted an e-commerce website on an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances behind an Application Load Balancer. The Solutions Architect noticed that the website is receiving a large number of illegitimate external requests from multiple systems with IP addresses that constantly change. To resolve the performance issues, the Solutions Architect must implement a solution that would block the illegitimate requests with&nbsp;minimal impact on legitimate traffic.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="647">Which of the following options fulfills this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10646" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10646" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a custom rule in the security group of the Application Load Balancer to block the offending requests.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10646" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a custom network ACL and associate it with the subnet of the Application Load Balancer to block the offending requests.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10646" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a rate-based rule in AWS WAF and associate the web ACL to an Application Load Balancer.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10646" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a regular rule in AWS WAF and associate the web ACL to an Application Load Balancer.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS WAF </strong>is tightly integrated with Amazon CloudFront, the Application Load Balancer (ALB), Amazon API Gateway, and AWS AppSync – services that AWS customers commonly use to deliver content for their websites and applications. When you use AWS WAF on Amazon CloudFront, your rules run in all AWS Edge Locations, located around the world close to your end-users. This means security doesn’t come at the expense of performance. Blocked requests are stopped before they reach your web servers. When you use AWS WAF on regional services, such as Application Load Balancer, Amazon API Gateway, and AWS AppSync, your rules run in the region and can be used to protect Internet-facing resources as well as internal resources.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/AWS-WAF-RateLimit.png" width="700" height="606"></p>
<p>A rate-based rule tracks the rate of requests for each originating IP address and triggers the rule action on IPs with rates that go over a limit. You set the limit as the number of requests per 5-minute time span. You can use this type of rule to put a temporary block on requests from an IP address that’s sending excessive requests.</p>
<p>Based on the given scenario, the requirement is to limit the number of requests from the illegitimate requests without affecting the genuine requests. To accomplish this requirement, you can use AWS WAF web ACL. There are two types of rules in creating your own web ACL rule: regular and rate-based rules. You need to select the latter to add a rate limit to your web ACL. After creating the web ACL, you can associate it with ALB. When the rule action triggers, AWS WAF applies the action to additional requests from the IP address until the request rate falls below the limit.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Create a rate-based rule in AWS WAF and associate the web ACL to an Application Load Balancer.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create a regular rule in AWS WAF and associate the web ACL to an Application Load Balancer </strong></span>is incorrect because a regular rule only matches the statement defined in the rule. If you need to add a rate limit to your rule, you should create a rate-based rule.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create a custom network ACL and associate it with the subnet of the Application Load Balancer to block the offending requests </strong></span>is incorrect. Although NACLs can help you block incoming traffic, this option wouldn’t be able to limit the number of requests from a single IP address that is dynamically changing.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create a custom rule in the security group of the Application Load Balancer to block the offending requests </strong></span>is incorrect because the security group can only allow incoming traffic. Remember that you can’t deny traffic using security groups. In addition, it is not capable of limiting the rate of traffic to your application unlike AWS WAF.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/waf/latest/developerguide/waf-rule-statement-type-rate-based.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/waf/latest/developerguide/waf-rule-statement-type-rate-based.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/waf/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/waf/faqs/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-waf/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-waf/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10723,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28954}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>29</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>29</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="207"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">A company has a web application that uses Amazon CloudFront to distribute its images, videos, and other static contents stored in its S3 bucket to its users around the world. The company has recently introduced a new member-only access feature to some of its high-quality media files. There is a requirement to provide access to multiple private media files only to their paying subscribers without having to change their current URLs. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="645"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">Which of the following is the most suitable solution that you should implement to satisfy this requirement?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10723" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10723" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure your CloudFront distribution to use Field-Level Encryption to protect your private data and only allow access to members.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10723" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a Signed URL with a custom policy which only allows the members to see the private files.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10723" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Use Signed Cookies to control who can access the private files in your CloudFront distribution by modifying your application to determine whether a user should have access to your content. For members, send the required <code>Set-Cookie</code> headers to the viewer which will unlock the content only to them.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10723" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure your CloudFront distribution to use Match Viewer as its Origin Protocol Policy which will automatically match the user request. This will allow access to the private content if the request is a paying member and deny it if it is not a member.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Many companies that distribute content over the internet want to restrict access to documents, business data, media streams, or content that is intended for selected users, for example, users who have paid a fee. To securely serve this private content by using CloudFront, you can do the following:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Require that your users access your private content by using special CloudFront signed URLs or signed cookies.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Require that your users access your content by using CloudFront URLs, not URLs that access content directly on the origin server (for example, Amazon S3 or a private HTTP server). Requiring CloudFront URLs isn’t necessary, but we recommend it to prevent users from bypassing the restrictions that you specify in signed URLs or signed cookies.</p>
<p>CloudFront signed URLs and signed cookies provide the same basic functionality: they allow you to control who can access your content.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-cloud-front-signed-URL-signed-Cookies.png" alt="" width="1000" height="637"></p>
<p>If you want to serve private content through CloudFront and you’re trying to decide whether to use signed URLs or signed cookies, consider the following:</p>
<p>Use <strong>signed URLs</strong>&nbsp;for the following cases:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You want to use an RTMP distribution. Signed cookies aren’t supported for RTMP distributions.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You want to restrict access to individual files, for example, an installation download for your application.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Your users are using a client (for example, a custom HTTP client) that doesn’t support cookies.</p>
<p>Use <strong>signed cookies</strong>&nbsp;for the following cases:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You want to provide access to multiple restricted files, for example, all of the files for a video in HLS format or all of the files in the subscribers’ area of a website.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You don’t want to change your current URLs.</p>
<div>
<p>Hence, the correct answer for this scenario is the option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use Signed Cookies to control who can access the private files in your CloudFront distribution by modifying your application to determine whether a user should have access to your content. For members, send the required <code>Set-Cookie</code> headers to the viewer which will unlock the content only to them.</strong></span></p>
</div>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configure your CloudFront distribution to use Match Viewer as its Origin Protocol Policy which will automatically match the user request. This will allow access to the private content if the request is a paying member and deny it if it is not a member</strong></span> is incorrect because a Match Viewer is an Origin Protocol Policy that configures CloudFront to communicate with your origin using HTTP or HTTPS, depending on the protocol of the viewer request. CloudFront caches the object only once even if viewers make requests using both HTTP and HTTPS protocols.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create a Signed URL with a custom policy which only allows the members to see the private files</strong></span> is incorrect because Signed URLs are primarily used for providing access to individual files, as shown in the above explanation. In addition, the scenario explicitly says that they don’t want to change their current URLs which is why implementing Signed Cookies is more suitable than Signed URLs.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configure your CloudFront distribution to use Field-Level Encryption to protect your private data and only allow access to members</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;Field-Level Encryption only allows you to securely upload user-submitted sensitive information to your web servers. It does not provide access to download multiple private files.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/private-content-choosing-signed-urls-cookies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/private-content-choosing-signed-urls-cookies.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/private-content-signed-cookies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/private-content-signed-cookies.html</a></p>

</p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>30</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>30</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A tech company has a CRM application hosted on an Auto Scaling group of On-Demand EC2 instances. The application is extensively used during office hours from 9 in the morning till 5 in the afternoon. Their users are complaining that the performance of the application is slow during the start of the day but then works normally after a couple of hours.</p>
<p>Which of the following can be done to ensure that the application works properly at the beginning of the day?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10632" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10632" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure a Dynamic scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances based on the Memory utilization.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10632" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an Application Load Balancer (ALB) to your architecture to ensure that the traffic is properly distributed on the instances.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10632" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure a Scheduled scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances before the start of the day.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10632" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure a Dynamic scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances based on the CPU utilization.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Scaling based on a schedule allows you to scale your application in response to predictable load changes. For example, every week the traffic to your web application starts to increase on Wednesday, remains high on Thursday, and starts to decrease on Friday. You can plan your scaling activities based on the predictable traffic patterns of your web application.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling-group.png" alt="" width="500" height="341"></p>
<p>To configure your Auto Scaling group to scale based on a schedule, you create a scheduled action. The scheduled action tells Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling to perform a scaling action at specified times. To create a scheduled scaling action, you specify the start time when the scaling action should take effect, and the new minimum, maximum, and desired sizes for the scaling action. At the specified time, Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling updates the group with the values for minimum, maximum, and desired size specified by the scaling action. You can create scheduled actions for scaling one time only or for scaling on a recurring schedule.</p>
<p>Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>configuring a Scheduled scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances before the start of the day</strong></span> is the correct answer. You need to configure a Scheduled scaling policy. This will ensure that the instances are already scaled up and ready before the start of the day since this is when the application is used the most.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configuring a Dynamic scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances based on the CPU utilization</strong></span> and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>configuring a Dynamic scaling policy for the Auto Scaling group to launch new instances based on the Memory utilization</strong></span> are both incorrect because although these are valid solutions, it is still better to configure a Scheduled scaling policy as you already know the exact peak hours of your application. By the time either the CPU or Memory hits a peak, the application already has performance issues, so you need to ensure the scaling is done beforehand using a Scheduled scaling policy.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Setting up an Application Load Balancer (ALB) to your architecture to ensure that the traffic is properly distributed on the instances</strong></span> is incorrect. Although the Application load balancer can also balance the traffic, it cannot increase the instances based on demand.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/schedule_time.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/schedule_time.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/</span></a></p>
</p>
