									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10648,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28946}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>31</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>31</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="205"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">A media company has an Amazon ECS Cluster, which uses the Fargate launch type, to host its news website. The application data are all stored in Amazon Keyspaces (for Apache Cassandra) with data-at-rest encryption enabled. The database credentials should be supplied using environment variables, to comply with strict security compliance. As the Solutions Architect, you have to ensure that the credentials are secure and that they cannot be viewed in plaintext on the cluster itself. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="691"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">Which of the following is the most suitable solution in this scenario that you can implement with minimal effort?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10648" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10648" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> In the ECS task definition file of the ECS Cluster, store the database credentials to Amazon ECS Anywhere to centrally manage these sensitive data and securely transmit it to only those containers that need access to it. Allocate an IAM Role to the cluster to ensure that the passwords are only accessible by the ECS service tasks. Run the  AWS IAM Access Analyzer to verify that the credentials can’t be viewed in plaintext.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10648" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Store the database credentials in the ECS task definition file of the ECS Cluster and encrypt it with KMS. Store the task definition JSON file in Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (Amazon QLDB). Create an IAM role to the ECS task definition script that allows access to the Amazon QLDB and then pass the <code>--cli-input-json</code> parameter when calling the ECS <code>register-task-definition</code> action. Reference the task definition JSON file in the Amazon QLDB which contains the database credentials.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10648" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Use the AWS Secrets Manager to store the database credentials and then encrypt them using AWS Certificate Manager (ACM). Create a resource-based policy for your Amazon ECS task execution role (<code>taskRoleArn</code>) and reference it with your task definition which allows access to both ACM and AWS Secrets Manager. Within your container definition, specify secrets with the name of the environment variable to set in the container and the full ARN of the Secrets Manager secret which contains the sensitive data, to present to the container.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10648" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Use the AWS Systems Manager Parameter Store to keep the database credentials and then encrypt them using AWS KMS. Create an IAM Role for your Amazon ECS task execution role (<code>taskRoleArn</code>) and reference it with your task definition, which allows access to both KMS and the Parameter Store. Within your container definition, specify secrets with the name of the environment variable to set in the container and the full ARN of the Systems Manager Parameter Store parameter containing the sensitive data to present to the container.</span>												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon ECS</strong> enables you to inject sensitive data into your containers by storing your sensitive data in either AWS Secrets Manager secrets or AWS Systems Manager Parameter Store parameters and then referencing them in your container definition. This feature is supported by tasks using both the EC2 and Fargate launch types.</p>
<p>Secrets can be exposed to a container in the following ways:</p>
<div>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– To inject sensitive data into your containers as environment variables, use the&nbsp;<code>secrets</code>&nbsp;container definition parameter.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– To reference sensitive information in the log configuration of a container, use the&nbsp;<code>&nbsp;container definition parameter.</code></p>
</div>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-systems-manager-parameter-store-securestring.png" alt="" width="1000" height="706"></p>
<p>Within your container definition, specify&nbsp;<code class="code">secrets</code>&nbsp;with the name of the environment variable to set in the container and the full ARN of either the Secrets Manager secret or Systems Manager Parameter Store parameter containing the sensitive data to present to the container. The parameter that you reference can be from a different Region than the container using it, but must be from within the same account.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is the option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use the AWS Systems Manager Parameter Store to keep the database credentials and then encrypt them using AWS KMS. Create an IAM Role for your Amazon ECS task execution role (<code>taskRoleArn</code>) and reference it with your task definition, which allows access to both KMS and the Parameter Store. Within your container definition, specify secrets with the name of the environment variable to set in the container and the full ARN of the Systems Manager Parameter Store parameter containing the sensitive data to present to the container</strong></span>.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>In the ECS task definition file of the ECS Cluster, store the database credentials to Amazon ECS Anywhere to centrally manage these sensitive data and securely transmit it to only those containers that need access to it. Allocate an IAM Role to the cluster to ensure that the passwords are only accessible by the ECS service tasks. Run the AWS IAM Access Analyzer to verify that the credentials can’t be viewed in plaintext</strong></span> is incorrect. Amazon Elastic Container Service (ECS) Anywhere is just a feature of Amazon ECS that enables you to easily run and manage container workloads on customer-managed infrastructure. This feature is not capable of storing any kind of credentials, let alone centrally manage your sensitive data. The recommended way to secure sensitive data in AWS is either through the use of Secrets Manager or Systems Manager Parameter Store. In addition, the AWS IAM Access Analyzer is primarily used to identify resources in your organization and accounts that are shared with an external entity, as well as to validate your IAM policies. This service can’t verify if your database credentials are viewable in plaintext or not.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Store the database credentials in the ECS task definition file of the ECS Cluster and encrypt it with KMS. Store the task definition JSON file in Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (Amazon QLDB). Create an IAM role to the ECS task definition script that allows access to the Amazon QLDB and then pass the <code>--cli-input-json</code> parameter when calling the ECS <code>register-task-definition</code> action. Reference the task definition JSON file in the Amazon QLDB which contains the database credentials</strong></span> is incorrect. Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (QLDB) is a fully managed ledger database that provides a transparent, immutable, and cryptographically verifiable transaction log. This service is not meant to store your sensitive database credentials.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use the AWS Secrets Manager to store the database credentials and then encrypt them using AWS Certificate Manager (ACM). Create a resource-based policy for your Amazon ECS task execution role (<code>taskRoleArn</code>) and reference it with your task definition which allows access to both ACM and AWS Secrets Manager. Within your container definition, specify secrets with the name of the environment variable to set in the container and the full ARN of the Secrets Manager secret which contains the sensitive data, to present to the container</strong></span> is incorrect. Although the use of Secrets Manager in securing sensitive data in ECS is valid, Amazon ECS doesn’t support resource-based policies. An example of a resource-based policy is the S3 bucket policy. An ECS task assumes an execution role (IAM role) to be able to call other AWS services like AWS Secrets Manager on your behalf. In addition, you cannot encrypt database credentials using the AWS Certificate Manager (ACM) service. You have to use AWS KMS instead.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECS/latest/developerguide/specifying-sensitive-data.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECS/latest/developerguide/specifying-sensitive-data.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECS/latest/developerguide/specifying-sensitive-data.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mt/the-right-way-to-store-secrets-using-parameter-store/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/systems-manager/latest/userguide/systems-manager-parameter-store.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/systems-manager/latest/userguide/systems-manager-parameter-store.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-systems-manager/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-systems-manager/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="multiple" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;multiple&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10122,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28979}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>32</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>32</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A popular social media website uses a CloudFront web distribution to serve their static contents to their millions of users around the globe. They are receiving a number of complaints recently that their users take a lot of time to log into their website. There are also occasions when their users are getting HTTP 504 errors. You are instructed by your manager to significantly reduce the user’s login time to further optimize the system.</p>
<p>Which of the following options should you use together to set up a cost-effective solution that can improve your application’s performance? (Select TWO.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10122" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10122" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Customize the content that the CloudFront web distribution delivers to your users using Lambda@Edge, which allows your Lambda functions to execute the authentication process in AWS locations closer to the users. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10122" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use multiple and geographically disperse VPCs to various AWS regions then create a transit VPC to connect all of your resources. In order to handle the requests faster, set up Lambda functions in each region using the AWS Serverless Application Model (SAM) service.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10122" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an origin failover by creating an origin group with two origins. Specify one as the primary origin and the other as the second origin which CloudFront automatically switches to when the primary origin returns specific HTTP status code failure responses.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10122" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Configure your origin to add a <code>Cache-Control max-age</code> directive to your objects, and specify the longest practical value for <code>max-age</code> to increase the cache hit ratio of your CloudFront distribution.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10122" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Deploy your application to multiple AWS regions to accommodate your users around the world. Set up a Route 53 record with latency routing policy to route incoming traffic to the region that provides the best latency to the user.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Lambda<a class="bp-suggestions-mention" href="https://portal.tutorialsdojo.com/members/edge/" rel="nofollow">@Edge</a> lets you run Lambda functions to customize the content that CloudFront delivers, executing the functions in AWS locations closer to the viewer. The functions run in response to CloudFront events, without provisioning or managing servers. You can use Lambda functions to change CloudFront requests and responses at the following points:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– After CloudFront receives a request from a viewer (viewer request)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Before CloudFront forwards the request to the origin (origin request)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– After CloudFront receives the response from the origin (origin response)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Before CloudFront forwards the response to the viewer (viewer response)</p>
<div>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/cloudfront-events-that-trigger-lambda-functions.png" alt="" width="545" height="194"></p>
</div>
<p>In the given scenario, you can use Lambda<a class="bp-suggestions-mention" href="https://portal.tutorialsdojo.com/members/edge/" rel="nofollow">@Edge</a> to allow your Lambda functions to customize the content that CloudFront delivers and to execute the authentication process in AWS locations closer to the users. In addition, you can set up an origin failover by creating an origin group with two origins with one as the primary origin and the other as the second origin which CloudFront automatically switches to when the primary origin fails. This will alleviate the occasional HTTP 504 errors that users are experiencing. Therefore, the correct answers are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Customize the content that the CloudFront web distribution delivers to your users using Lambda<a class="bp-suggestions-mention" href="https://portal.tutorialsdojo.com/members/edge/" rel="nofollow">@Edge</a>, which allows your Lambda functions to execute the authentication process in AWS locations closer to the users.</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>–&nbsp;Set up an origin failover by creating an origin group with two origins. Specify one as the primary origin and the other as the second origin which CloudFront automatically switches to when the primary origin returns specific HTTP status code failure responses.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use multiple and geographically disperse VPCs to various AWS regions then create a transit VPC to connect all of your resources. In order to handle the requests faster, set up Lambda functions in each region using the AWS Serverless Application Model (SAM) service</strong></span> is incorrect because of the same reason provided above. Although setting up multiple VPCs across various regions which&nbsp;are connected with a transit VPC is valid, this solution still entails higher setup and maintenance costs. A more cost-effective option would be to use Lambda<a class="bp-suggestions-mention" href="https://portal.tutorialsdojo.com/members/edge/" rel="nofollow">@Edge</a> instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configure your origin to add a <code>Cache-Control max-age</code> directive to your objects, and specify the longest practical value for <code>max-age</code> to increase the cache hit ratio of your CloudFront distribution</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;improving the cache hit ratio for the CloudFront distribution is irrelevant in this scenario. You can improve your cache performance by increasing the proportion of your viewer requests that are served from CloudFront edge caches instead of going to your origin servers for content. However, take note that the problem in the scenario is the sluggish authentication process of your global users and not just the caching of the static objects.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Deploy your application to multiple AWS regions to accommodate your users around the world. Set up a Route 53 record with latency routing policy to route incoming traffic to the region that provides the best latency to the user</strong></span> is incorrect. Although this may resolve the performance issue, this solution entails a significant implementation cost since you have to deploy your application to multiple AWS regions. Remember that the scenario asks for a solution that will&nbsp;improve the performance of the application with <strong>minimal cost</strong>.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/high_availability_origin_failover.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudFront/latest/DeveloperGuide/high_availability_origin_failover.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/lambda-edge.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/lambda-edge.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-lambda/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-lambda/</a></p>
</p>

											</li>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>33</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>33</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Applications and Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="180">A business has recently migrated its applications to AWS. The audit team must be able to assess whether the services the company is using meet common security and regulatory standards. A solutions architect needs to provide the team with a report of all compliance-related documents for their account.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="483">&nbsp;Which action should a solutions architect consider?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10445" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10445" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Run an Amazon Macie job to view the Service Organization Control (SOC), Payment Card Industry (PCI), and other compliance reports from AWS Certificate Manager (ACM).												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10445" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Run an Amazon Inspector assessment job to download all of the AWS compliance-related information.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10445" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> View all of the AWS security compliance reports from AWS Security Hub.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10445" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Artifact to view the security reports as well as other AWS compliance-related information. 												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS Artifact</strong> is your go-to, central resource for compliance-related information that matters to you. It provides on-demand access to AWS’ security and compliance reports and select online agreements. Reports available in AWS Artifact include our Service Organization Control (SOC) reports, Payment Card Industry (PCI) reports, and certifications from accreditation bodies across geographies and compliance verticals that validate the implementation and operating effectiveness of AWS security controls. Agreements available in AWS Artifact include the Business Associate Addendum (BAA) and the Nondisclosure Agreement (NDA).</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-artifact-console.jpg" alt="" width="700" height="366"></p>
<p>All AWS Accounts have access to AWS Artifact. Root users and IAM users with admin permissions can download all audit artifacts available to their accounts by agreeing to the associated terms and conditions. You will need to grant IAM users with non-admin permissions access to AWS Artifact using IAM permissions. This allows you to grant a user access to AWS Artifact while restricting access to other services and resources within your AWS Account.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is:&nbsp;<strong><span style="color: #008000;">Use AWS Artifact to view the security reports as well as other AWS compliance-related information.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Run an Amazon Inspector assessment job to download all of the AWS compliance-related information</strong>&nbsp;</span>is incorrect. Amazon Inspector is simply a security tool for detecting vulnerabilities in AWS workloads. For this scenario, it is better to use the readily-available security reports in AWS Artifact instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Run an Amazon Macie job to view the Service Organization Control (SOC), Payment Card Industry (PCI), and other compliance reports from AWS Certificate Manager (ACM)</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because ACM is just a service that lets you easily provision, manage, and deploy public and private Secure Sockets Layer/Transport Layer Security (SSL/TLS) certificates for use with AWS services and your internal connected resources. This service does not store certifications or compliance-related documents.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>View all of the AWS security compliance reports from AWS Security Hub</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;AWS Security Hub only provides you a comprehensive view of your high-priority security alerts and security posture across your AWS accounts.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/artifact/getting-started/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/artifact/getting-started/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/artifact/latest/ug/what-is-aws-artifact.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/artifact/latest/ug/what-is-aws-artifact.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10374,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29019}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>34</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>34</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="195"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A car dealership website hosted in Amazon EC2 stores car listings in an Amazon Aurora database managed by Amazon RDS. Once a vehicle has been sold, its data must be removed from the current listings and forwarded to a&nbsp;distributed processing system.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="445"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Which of the following options can satisfy the given requirement?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10374" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10374" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a native function or a stored procedure that invokes a Lambda function. Configure the Lambda function to send event notifications to an Amazon SQS queue for the processing system to consume. 
												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10374" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to AWS Lambda. Configure the Lambda function to fan out the event notifications to multiple Amazon SQS queues to update the processing system.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10374" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to AWS Lambda. Configure the Lambda function to fanout the event notifications to multiple Amazon SQS queues to update the target groups.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10374" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to Amazon SQS. Configure the SQS queues to fan out the event notifications to multiple Amazon SNS topics. Process the data using Lambda functions.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>You can invoke an AWS Lambda function from an Amazon Aurora MySQL-Compatible Edition DB cluster with a native function or a stored procedure.&nbsp;This approach can be useful when you want to integrate your database running on Aurora MySQL with other AWS services. For example, you might want to capture data changes whenever a row in a table is modified in your database.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-aurora-native-functions.png" alt="" width="450" height="268"></p>
<p>In the scenario, you can trigger a Lambda function whenever a listing is deleted from the database. You can then write the logic of the function to send the listing data to an SQS queue and have different processes consume it.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Create a native function or a stored procedure that invokes a Lambda function. Configure the Lambda function to send event notifications to an Amazon SQS queue for the processing system to consume.</strong></span></p>
<p>RDS events only provide operational events such as DB instance events, DB parameter group events, DB security group events, and DB snapshot events. What we need in the scenario is to capture data-modifying events (<code>INSERT</code>, <code>DELETE</code>, <code>UPDATE</code>) which can be achieved thru native functions or stored procedures. Hence, the following options are incorrect:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>– Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to Amazon SQS. Configure the SQS queues to fan out the event notifications to multiple Amazon SNS topics. Process the data using Lambda functions.</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>– Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to AWS Lambda. Configure the Lambda function to fan out the event notifications to multiple Amazon SQS queues to update the processing system.</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>– Create an RDS event subscription and send the notifications to Amazon SNS. Configure the SNS topic to fan out the event notifications to multiple Amazon SQS queues. Process the data using Lambda functions.</strong></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/AuroraMySQL.Integrating.Lambda.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/AuroraMySQL.Integrating.Lambda.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/database/capturing-data-changes-in-amazon-aurora-using-aws-lambda/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/database/capturing-data-changes-in-amazon-aurora-using-aws-lambda/</a></p>

						<div style="clear: both;"></div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:7422,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28995}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>35</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>35</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="189"><span data-renderer-mark="true">An application consists of multiple EC2 instances in private subnets in different availability zones.</span> The application uses a single NAT Gateway for downloading software patches from the Internet to the instances. There is a requirement to protect the application from a single point of failure when the NAT Gateway encounters a failure or if its availability zone goes down.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="565">How should the Solutions Architect redesign the architecture to be more highly available and cost-effective?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="7422" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7422" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create two NAT Gateways in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each public subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7422" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a NAT Gateway in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each public subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7422" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create three NAT Gateways in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each private subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_7422" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a NAT Gateway in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each private subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">A <strong>NAT Gateway</strong> is a highly available, managed Network Address Translation (NAT) service for your resources in a private subnet to access the Internet</span><span style="font-weight: 400;">. NAT gateway is created in a specific Availability Zone and implemented with redundancy in that zone.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">You must create a NAT gateway on a public subnet to enable instances in a private subnet to connect to the Internet or other AWS services, but prevent the Internet from initiating a connection with those instances.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/images/nat-gateway-diagram.png" alt="" width="738" height="559"></span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">If you have resources in multiple Availability Zones and they share one NAT gateway, and if the NAT gateway’s Availability Zone is down, resources in the other Availability Zones lose Internet access. To create an Availability Zone-independent architecture, create a NAT gateway in each Availability Zone and configure your routing to ensure that resources use the NAT gateway in the same Availability Zone.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Hence, the correct answer is:&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Create a NAT Gateway in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each private subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create a NAT Gateway in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each public subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone</strong></span> <span style="font-weight: 400;">is incorrect because you should configure the route table in the private subnet and not the public subnet to associate the right instances in the private subnet.</span></p>
<p>The options that say:<strong>&nbsp; <span style="color: #ff6600;">Create two NAT Gateways in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each public subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone</span></strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and </span><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Create three NAT Gateways in each availability zone. Configure the route table in each private subnet to ensure that instances use the NAT Gateway in the same availability zone</span> </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">are both</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> incorrect because a single NAT Gateway in each availability zone is enough. NAT Gateway is already redundant in nature, meaning, AWS already handles any failures that occur in your NAT Gateway in an availability zone.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/vpc-nat-gateway.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/vpc-nat-gateway.html</a></span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/vpc-nat-comparison.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/vpc-nat-comparison.html</a></span></p>

</p>
								</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10078,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28917}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>36</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>36</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An application that records weather data every minute is deployed in a fleet of Spot EC2 instances and uses a MySQL RDS database instance. Currently, there is only one RDS instance running in one Availability Zone. You plan to improve the database to ensure high availability by synchronous data replication to another RDS instance.</p>
<p>Which of the following performs synchronous data replication in RDS?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10078" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10078" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> DynamoDB Read Replica												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10078" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> CloudFront running as a Multi-AZ deployment												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10078" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> RDS DB instance running as a Multi-AZ deployment												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10078" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> RDS Read Replica												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>When you create or modify your DB instance to run as a Multi-AZ deployment, Amazon RDS automatically provisions and maintains a synchronous <strong>standby&nbsp;</strong>replica in a different Availability Zone. Updates to your DB Instance are synchronously replicated across Availability Zones to the standby in order to keep both in sync and protect your latest database updates against DB instance failure.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-06-07_10-00-40-e7c750751ea701ec7b91cbeeb464f364.png" alt="" width="700" height="226"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>RDS Read Replica</strong></span> is incorrect as a Read Replica provides an asynchronous replication instead of synchronous.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>DynamoDB Read Replica</strong></span> and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>CloudFront running as a Multi-AZ deployment</strong></span> are incorrect as both DynamoDB and CloudFront do not have a Read Replica feature.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10677,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28891}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>37</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>37</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A financial application is composed of an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances, an Application Load Balancer, and a MySQL RDS instance in a Multi-AZ Deployments configuration. To protect the confidential data of your customers, you have to ensure that your RDS database can only be accessed using the profile credentials specific to your EC2 instances via an authentication token.</p>
<p>As the Solutions Architect of the company, which of the following should you do to meet the above requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10677" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10677" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable the IAM DB Authentication.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10677" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure SSL in your application to encrypt the database connection to RDS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10677" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use a combination of IAM and STS to restrict access to your RDS instance via a temporary token.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10677" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an IAM Role and assign it to your EC2 instances which will grant exclusive access to your RDS instance.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>You can authenticate to your DB&nbsp;instance&nbsp;using AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM) database authentication. IAM database authentication works with MySQL and PostgreSQL. With this authentication method, you don’t need to use a password when you connect to a DB instance. Instead, you use an authentication token.</p>
<p>An&nbsp;<strong><em>authentication token</em></strong>&nbsp;is a unique string of characters that&nbsp;Amazon RDS&nbsp;generates on request. Authentication tokens are generated using AWS Signature Version 4. Each token has a lifetime of 15 minutes. You don’t need to store user credentials in the database, because authentication is managed externally using IAM. You can also still use standard database authentication.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-01-13_07-04-06-a2157247b0fa129795001208504fcb51.png" width="750" height="830"></p>
<p>IAM database authentication provides the following benefits:</p>
<div>
<ol type="disc">
<li>Network traffic to and from the database is encrypted using Secure Sockets Layer (SSL).</li>
<li>You can use IAM to centrally manage access to your database resources, instead of managing access individually on each DB&nbsp;instance.</li>
<li>For applications running on Amazon EC2, you can use profile credentials specific to your EC2 instance to access your database instead of a password, for greater security</li>
</ol>
<p>Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>enabling IAM DB Authentication</strong></span> is the correct answer based on the above reference.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configuring SSL in your application to encrypt the database connection to RDS</strong></span> is incorrect because an SSL connection is not using an authentication token from IAM. Although configuring SSL to your application can improve the security of your data in flight, it is still not a suitable option to use in this scenario.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Creating an IAM Role and assigning it to your EC2 instances which will grant exclusive access to your RDS instance</strong></span> is incorrect because although you can create and assign an IAM Role to your EC2 instances, you still need to configure your RDS to use IAM DB Authentication.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using a combination of IAM and STS to restrict access to your RDS instance via a temporary token</strong></span> is incorrect because you have to use IAM DB Authentication for this scenario, and not a combination of an IAM and STS. Although STS is used to send temporary tokens for authentication, this is not a compatible use case for RDS.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/UsingWithRDS.IAMDBAuth.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/UsingWithRDS.IAMDBAuth.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

</div>
</p>
								</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10601,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28967}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>38</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>38</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Applications and Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="191">A company uses an Application Load Balancer (ALB) for its public-facing multi-tier web applications. The security team has recently reported that there has been a surge of SQL injection attacks lately, which causes critical data discrepancy issues. The same issue is also encountered by its other web applications in other AWS accounts that are behind an ALB. An immediate solution is required to prevent the remote injection of unauthorized SQL queries and protect their applications hosted across multiple accounts.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="710">As a Solutions Architect, what solution would you recommend?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10601" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10601" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon GuardDuty and set up a managed rule to block request patterns associated with the exploitation of SQL databases, like SQL injection attacks. Associate it with the Application Load Balancer and utilize the AWS Security Hub service to reuse the managed rules across all the AWS accounts												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10601" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Network Firewall to filter web vulnerabilities and brute force attacks using stateful rule groups across all Application Load Balancers on all AWS accounts. Refactor the web application to be less susceptible to SQL injection attacks based on the security assessment.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10601" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS WAF and set up a managed rule to block request patterns associated with the exploitation of SQL databases, like SQL injection attacks. Associate it with the Application Load Balancer. Integrate AWS WAF with AWS Firewall Manager to reuse the rules across all the AWS accounts.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10601" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon Macie to scan for vulnerabilities and unintended network exposure. Refactor the web application to be less susceptible to SQL injection attacks based on the security assessment. Utilize the AWS Audit Manager to reuse the security assessment across all AWS accounts.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS WAF</strong> is a web application firewall that lets you monitor the HTTP(S) requests that are forwarded to an Amazon CloudFront distribution, an Amazon API Gateway REST API, an Application Load Balancer, or an AWS AppSync GraphQL API.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>-Web ACLs</strong> – You use a web access control list (ACL) to protect a set of AWS resources. You create a web ACL and define its protection strategy by adding rules. Rules define criteria for inspecting web requests and specify how to handle requests that match the criteria. You set a default action for the web ACL that indicates whether to block or allow through those requests that pass the rules inspections.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>-Rules</strong> – Each rule contains a statement that defines the inspection criteria and an action to take if a web request meets the criteria. When a web request meets the criteria, that’s a match. You can configure rules to block matching requests, allow them through, count them, or run CAPTCHA controls against them.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>-Rules groups</strong> – You can use rules individually or in reusable rule groups. AWS Managed Rules and AWS Marketplace sellers provide managed rule groups for your use. You can also define your own rule groups.</p>
<p><strong>AWSManagedRulesSQLiRuleSet</strong> – The SQL database rule group contains rules to block request patterns associated with the exploitation of SQL databases, like SQL injection attacks. This can help prevent remote injection of unauthorized queries. Evaluate this rule group for use if your application interfaces with an SQL database.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-waf-sql-injection-attack-prevention.png" alt="" width="1000" height="585"></p>
<p>AWS WAF is easy to deploy and protect applications deployed on either Amazon CloudFront as part of your CDN solution, the Application Load Balancer that fronts all your origin servers, Amazon API Gateway for your REST APIs, or AWS AppSync for your GraphQL APIs. There is no additional software to deploy, DNS configuration, SSL/TLS certificate to manage, or need for a reverse proxy setup.</p>
<p>With AWS Firewall Manager integration, you can centrally define and manage your rules and reuse them across all the web applications that you need to protect.</p>
<p>Therefore, the correct answer is:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use AWS WAF and set up a managed rule to block request patterns associated with the exploitation of SQL databases, like SQL injection attacks. Associate it with the Application Load Balancer. Integrate AWS WAF with AWS Firewall Manager to reuse the rules across all the AWS accounts.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use Amazon GuardDuty and set up a managed rule to block request patterns associated with the exploitation of SQL databases, like SQL injection attacks. Associate it with the Application Load Balancer and utilize the AWS Security Hub service to reuse the managed rules across all the AWS accounts</strong></span>is incorrect because Amazon GuardDuty is only a threat detection service and cannot directly be integrated with the Application Load Balancer.</p>
<p>The options that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Network Firewall to filter web vulnerabilities and brute force attacks using stateful rule groups across all Application Load Balancers on all AWS accounts. Refactor the web application to be less susceptible to SQL injection attacks based on the security assessment</strong></span>is incorrect because AWS Network Firewall is a managed service that is primarily used to deploy essential network protections for all of your Amazon Virtual Private Clouds (VPCs) and not particularly to your Application Load Balancers. Take note that the AWS Network Firewall is account-specific by default and needs to be integrated with the AWS Firewall Manager to easily share the firewall across your other AWS accounts. In addition, refactoring the web application will require an immense amount of time.</p>
<p>The options that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use Amazon Macie to scan for vulnerabilities and unintended network exposure. Refactor the web application to be less susceptible to SQL injection attacks based on the security assessment. Utilize the AWS Audit Manager to reuse the security assessment across all AWS accounts </strong></span>is incorrect because Amazon Macie is only used for data security and data privacy service that uses machine learning and pattern matching to discover and protect your sensitive data. Just like before, refactoring the web application will require an immense amount of time. The use of the AWS Audit Manager is not relevant as well. The AWS Audit Manager simply helps you continually audit your AWS usage to simplify how you manage risk and compliance with regulations and industry standards.</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/waf/latest/developerguide/fms-chapter.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/waf/latest/developerguide/fms-chapter.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->

							Question <span>39</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>39</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>There was an incident in your production environment where the user data stored in the S3 bucket has been accidentally deleted by one of the Junior DevOps Engineers. The issue was escalated to your manager and after a few days, you were instructed to improve the security and protection of your AWS resources.</p>
<p>What combination of the following options will protect the S3 objects in your bucket from both accidental deletion and overwriting? (Select TWO.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="2414" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_2414" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Provide access to S3 data strictly through pre-signed URL only												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_2414" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Multi-Factor Authentication Delete												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_2414" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_2414" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Disallow S3 Delete using an IAM bucket policy												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_2414" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Versioning												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p style="text-align: left;">By using Versioning and enabling MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication) Delete, you can secure and recover your S3 objects from accidental deletion or overwrite.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Versioning is a means of keeping multiple variants of an object in the same bucket. Versioning-enabled buckets enable you to recover objects from accidental deletion or overwrite. You can use versioning to preserve, retrieve, and restore every version of every object stored in your Amazon S3 bucket. With versioning, you can easily recover from both unintended user actions and application failures.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">You can also optionally add another layer of security by configuring a bucket to enable MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication) Delete, which requires additional authentication for either of the following operations:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">– Change the versioning state of your bucket</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">– Permanently delete an object version</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">MFA Delete requires two forms of authentication together:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">– Your security credentials</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">– The concatenation of a valid serial number, a space, and the six-digit code displayed on an approved authentication device</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Providing access to S3 data strictly through pre-signed URL only</strong></span> is incorrect since a pre-signed URL gives access to the object identified in the URL. Pre-signed URLs are useful when customers perform an object upload to your S3&nbsp;bucket, but does not help in preventing accidental deletes.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Disallowing S3 Delete using an IAM bucket policy</strong></span> is incorrect since you still want users to be able to delete objects in the bucket, and you just want to prevent accidental deletions.&nbsp;Disallowing S3 Delete using an IAM bucket policy will restrict all delete operations to your bucket.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enabling Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering</strong></span> is incorrect since S3 intelligent tiering does not help in this situation.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>Reference:&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Versioning.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Versioning.html</a></p>
