									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="multiple" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;multiple&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10715,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29001}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>40</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>40</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="205"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">A government agency plans to store confidential tax documents on AWS. Due to the sensitive information in the files, the Solutions Architect must restrict the data access requests made to the storage solution to a specific Amazon VPC only. The solution should also prevent the files from being deleted or overwritten to meet the regulatory requirement of having a write-once-read-many (WORM) storage model.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="613"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">Which combination of the following options should the Architect implement? (Select TWO.)</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10715" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10715" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a new Amazon S3 bucket to store the tax documents and integrate it with AWS Network Firewall. Configure the Network Firewall to only accept data access requests from a specific Amazon VPC. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10715" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a new Amazon S3 bucket with the S3 Object Lock feature enabled. Store the documents in the bucket and set the Legal Hold option for object retention.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10715" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Store the tax documents in the Amazon S3 Glacier Instant Retrieval storage class to restrict fast data retrieval to a particular Amazon VPC of your choice.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10715" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure an Amazon S3 Access Point for the S3 bucket to restrict data access to a particular Amazon VPC only. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10715" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Object Lock but disable Object Versioning on the new Amazon S3 bucket to comply with the write-once-read-many (WORM) storage model requirement.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Amazon S3 access points simplify data access for any AWS service or customer application that stores data in S3. Access points are named network endpoints that are attached to buckets that you can use to perform S3 object operations, such as&nbsp;<code>GetObject</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code>PutObject</code>.</p>
<p>Each access point has distinct permissions and network controls that S3 applies for any request that is made through that access point. Each access point enforces a customized access point policy that works in conjunction with the bucket policy that is attached to the underlying bucket. You can configure any access point to accept requests only from a virtual private cloud (VPC) to restrict Amazon S3 data access to a private network. You can also configure custom block public access settings for each access point.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3-access-points-via-vpc.png" alt="" width="1200" height="782"></p>
<p>You can also use Amazon S3 Multi-Region Access Points to provide a global endpoint that applications can use to fulfill requests from S3 buckets located in multiple AWS Regions. You can use Multi-Region Access Points to build multi-Region applications with the same simple architecture used in a single Region, and then run those applications anywhere in the world. Instead of sending requests over the congested public internet, Multi-Region Access Points provide built-in network resilience with acceleration of internet-based requests to Amazon S3. Application requests made to a Multi-Region Access Point global endpoint use AWS Global Accelerator to automatically route over the AWS global network to the S3 bucket with the lowest network latency.</p>
<p>With S3 Object Lock, you can store objects using a write-once-read-many (WORM) model. Object Lock can help prevent objects from being deleted or overwritten for a fixed amount of time or indefinitely. You can use Object Lock to help meet regulatory requirements that require WORM storage, or to simply add another layer of protection against object changes and deletion.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3-object-lock-with-bucket-versioning.png" alt="" width="1200" height="1100"></p>
<p>Before you lock any objects, you have to enable a bucket to use S3 Object Lock. You enable Object Lock when you create a bucket. After you enable Object Lock on a bucket, you can lock objects in that bucket. When you create a bucket with Object Lock enabled, you can’t disable Object Lock or suspend versioning for that bucket.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answers are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Configure an Amazon S3 Access Point for the S3 bucket to restrict data access to a particular Amazon VPC only.</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Create a new Amazon S3 bucket with the S3 Object Lock feature enabled. Store the documents in the bucket and set the Legal Hold option for object retention.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a new Amazon S3 bucket to store the tax documents and integrate it with AWS Network Firewall. Configure the Network Firewall to only accept data access requests from a specific Amazon VPC</strong></span> is incorrect because you cannot directly use an AWS Network Firewall to restrict S3 bucket data access requests to a specific Amazon VPC only. You have to use an Amazon S3 Access Point instead for this particular use case. An AWS Network Firewall is commonly integrated to your Amazon VPC and not to an S3 bucket.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Store the tax documents in the Amazon S3 Glacier Instant Retrieval storage class to restrict fast data retrieval to a particular Amazon VPC of your choice</strong></span> is incorrect because Amazon S3 Glacier Instant Retrieval is just an archive storage class that delivers the lowest-cost storage for long-lived data that is rarely accessed and requires retrieval in milliseconds. It neither provides write-once-read-many (WORM) storage nor a fine-grained network control that restricts S3 bucket access to a specific Amazon VPC.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Enable Object Lock but disable Object Versioning on the new Amazon S3 bucket to comply with the write-once-read-many (WORM) storage model requirement</strong></span> is incorrect. Although the Object Lock feature does provide write-once-read-many (WORM) storage, the Object Versioning feature must also be enabled too in order for this to work. In fact, you cannot manually disable the Object Versioning feature if you have already selected the Object Lock option.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/access-points.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/access-points.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/object-lock.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/object-lock.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>41</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>41</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A Solutions Architect is working for a company which has multiple VPCs in various AWS regions. The Architect is assigned to set up a logging system which will track all of the changes made to their AWS resources in all regions, including the configurations made in IAM, CloudFront, AWS WAF, and Route 53. In order to pass the compliance requirements, the solution must ensure the security, integrity, and durability of the log data. It should also provide an event history of all API calls made in AWS Management Console and AWS CLI.</p>
<p>Which of the following solutions is the best fit for this scenario?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10084" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10084" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up a new CloudWatch trail in a new S3 bucket using the CloudTrail console and also pass the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> parameter then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10084" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up a new CloudWatch trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10084" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up a new CloudTrail trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--no-include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10084" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up a new CloudTrail trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies.</span>												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>An <strong>event</strong> in CloudTrail is the record of an activity in an AWS account. This activity can be an action taken by a user, role, or service that is monitorable by CloudTrail. CloudTrail events provide a history of both API and non-API account activity made through the AWS Management Console, AWS SDKs, command-line tools, and other AWS services. There are two types of events that can be logged in CloudTrail: management events and data events. By default, trails log management events, but not data events.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/cloudtrail_all_regions_main_screen_turn_on_1.png" alt="" width="700" height="454"></p>
<p>A trail can be applied to all regions or a single region. As a best practice, create a trail that applies to all regions in the AWS partition in which you are working. This is the default setting when you create a trail in the CloudTrail console.</p>
<p>For most services, events are recorded in the region where the action occurred. For global services such as AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM), AWS STS, Amazon CloudFront, and Route 53, events are delivered to any trail that includes global services, and are logged as occurring in US East (N. Virginia) Region.</p>
<p>In this scenario, the company requires a secure and durable logging solution that will track all of the activities of all AWS resources in all regions. CloudTrail can be used for this case with multi-region trail enabled, however, it will only cover the activities of the regional services (EC2, S3, RDS etc.) and not for global services such as IAM, CloudFront, AWS WAF, and Route 53. In order to satisfy the requirement, you have to add the <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameter in your AWS CLI command.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Set up a new CloudTrail trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies</strong></span> is correct because it provides security, integrity, and durability to your log data and in addition, it has the -include-global-service-events parameter enabled which will also include activity from global services such as IAM, Route 53, AWS WAF, and CloudFront.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a new CloudWatch trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies</strong></span> is incorrect because you need to use CloudTrail instead of CloudWatch.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a new CloudWatch trail in a new S3 bucket using the CloudTrail console and also pass the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> parameter then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies</strong></span> is incorrect because you need to use CloudTrail instead of CloudWatch. In addition, the –include-global-service-events parameter is also missing in this setup.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a new CloudTrail trail in a new S3 bucket using the AWS CLI and also pass both the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> and <code>--no-include-global-service-events</code> parameters then encrypt log files using KMS encryption. Apply Multi Factor Authentication (MFA) Delete on the S3 bucket and ensure that only authorized users can access the logs by configuring the bucket policies</strong></span> is incorrect because the <code>--is-multi-region-trail</code> is not enough as you also need to add the <code>--include-global-service-events</code> parameter and not <code>--no-include-global-service-events</code>.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/cloudtrail-integration.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">http://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/cloudtrail-integration.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/awscloudtrail/latest/userguide/cloudtrail-create-and-update-a-trail-by-using-the-aws-cli.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/awscloudtrail/latest/userguide/cloudtrail-create-and-update-a-trail-by-using-the-aws-cli.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>42</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>42</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="217"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">A tech company that you are working for has undertaken a Total Cost Of Ownership (TCO) analysis evaluating the use of Amazon S3 versus acquiring more storage hardware. The result was that all 1200 employees would be granted access to use Amazon S3 for the storage of their personal documents. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="512"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">Which of the following will you need to consider so you can set up a solution that incorporates a single sign-on feature from your corporate AD or LDAP directory and also restricts access for each individual user to a designated user folder in an S3 bucket? (Select TWO.)</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10661" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10661" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a matching IAM user for each of the 1200 users in your corporate directory that needs access to a folder in the S3 bucket.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10661" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure an IAM role and an IAM Policy to access the bucket.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10661" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Map each individual user to a designated user folder in S3 using Amazon WorkDocs to access their personal documents.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10661" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a Federation proxy or an Identity provider, and use AWS Security Token Service to generate temporary tokens.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10661" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use 3rd party Single Sign-On solutions such as Atlassian Crowd, OKTA, OneLogin and many others.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>The question refers to one of the common scenarios for temporary credentials in AWS. Temporary credentials are useful in scenarios that involve identity federation, delegation, cross-account access, and IAM roles. In this example, it is called <strong>enterprise identity federation</strong> considering that you also need to set up a&nbsp;single sign-on (SSO) capability.</p>
<p>The correct answers are:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Setup a Federation proxy or an Identity provider</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>– Setup an AWS Security Token Service to generate temporary tokens&nbsp;</strong></span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>–&nbsp;Configure an IAM role and an IAM Policy to access the bucket.&nbsp;</strong></span></p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/saml-based-federation.diagram.png" width="700" height="393">In an enterprise identity federation, you can authenticate users in your organization’s network, and then provide those users access to AWS without creating new AWS identities for them and requiring them to sign in with a separate user name and password. This is known as the&nbsp;<em>single sign-on</em>&nbsp;(SSO) approach to temporary access. AWS STS supports open standards like Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML) 2.0, with which you can use Microsoft AD FS to leverage your Microsoft Active Directory. You can also use SAML 2.0 to manage your own solution for federating user identities.</p>
<p><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">Using 3rd party Single Sign-On solutions such as Atlassian Crowd, OKTA, OneLogin and many others</span>&nbsp;</strong>is incorrect since you don’t have to use 3rd party solutions to provide the access. AWS already provides the necessary tools that you can use in this situation.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Mapping each individual user to a designated user folder in S3 using Amazon WorkDocs to access their personal documents</strong></span> is incorrect as there is no direct way of integrating Amazon S3 with Amazon WorkDocs for this particular scenario.&nbsp;Amazon WorkDocs is simply a fully managed, secure content creation, storage, and collaboration service. With Amazon WorkDocs, you can easily create, edit, and share content. And because it’s stored centrally on AWS, you can access it from anywhere on any device.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Setting up a matching IAM user for each of the 1200 users in your corporate directory that needs access to a folder in the S3 bucket</strong></span> is incorrect since creating that many IAM users would be unnecessary. Also, you want the account to integrate with your AD or LDAP directory, hence, IAM Users does not fit these criteria.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_saml.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_saml.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_oidc.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_roles_providers_oidc.html</a></p>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10680,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28958}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>43</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>43</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="203"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A Solutions Architect identified a series of DDoS attacks while monitoring the VPC. The Architect needs to fortify the current cloud infrastructure to protect the data of the clients. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="389"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Which of the following is the most suitable solution to mitigate these kinds of attacks?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10680" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10680" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> A combination of Security Groups and Network Access Control Lists to only allow authorized traffic to access your VPC.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10680" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a web application firewall using AWS WAF to filter, monitor, and block HTTP traffic.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10680" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Using the AWS Firewall Manager, set up a security layer that will prevent SYN floods, UDP reflection attacks, and other DDoS attacks.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10680" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Shield Advanced to detect and mitigate DDoS attacks.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>For higher levels of protection against attacks targeting your applications running on Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2), Elastic Load Balancing(ELB), Amazon CloudFront, and Amazon Route 53 resources, you can subscribe to AWS Shield Advanced. In addition to the network and transport layer protections that come with Standard, AWS Shield Advanced provides additional detection and mitigation against large and sophisticated DDoS attacks, near real-time visibility into attacks, and integration with AWS WAF, a web application firewall.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/web-app-ddos-mitigation.4fc1b1d10a6e8517dcd80547544c1ee4f423da1b.png" width="550" height="199"></p>
<p><strong>AWS Shield Advanced</strong> also gives you 24×7 access to the AWS DDoS Response Team (DRT) and protection against DDoS related spikes in your Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2), Elastic Load Balancing(ELB), Amazon CloudFront, and Amazon Route 53 charges.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use AWS Shield Advanced to detect and mitigate DDoS attacks.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using the AWS Firewall Manager, set up a security layer that will prevent SYN floods, UDP reflection attacks and other DDoS attacks</strong></span> is incorrect because AWS Firewall Manager is mainly used to simplify your AWS WAF administration and maintenance tasks across multiple accounts and resources. It does not protect your VPC against DDoS attacks.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a web application firewall using AWS WAF to filter, monitor, and block HTTP traffic</strong></span> is incorrect. Even though AWS WAF can help you block common attack patterns to your VPC such as SQL injection or cross-site scripting, this is still not enough to withstand DDoS attacks. It is better to use AWS Shield in this scenario.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>A combination of Security Groups and Network Access Control Lists to only allow authorized traffic to access your VPC</strong></span> is incorrect. Although using a combination of Security Groups and NACLs are valid to provide security to your VPC, this is not enough to mitigate a DDoS attack. You should use AWS Shield for better security protection.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://d1.awsstatic.com/whitepapers/Security/DDoS_White_Paper.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://d1.awsstatic.com/whitepapers/Security/DDoS_White_Paper.pdf</a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/shield/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/shield/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="multiple" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;multiple&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10613,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28977}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>44</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>44</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="215">An online learning company hosts its Microsoft .NET e-Learning application on a Windows Server in its on-premises data center. The application uses an Oracle Database Standard Edition as its backend database.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="426">The company wants a high-performing solution to migrate this workload to the AWS cloud to take advantage of the cloud’s high availability. The migration process should minimize development changes, and the environment should be easier to manage.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="673">Which of the following options should be implemented to meet the company requirements? (Select TWO.)</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10613" data-type="multiple">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10613" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Rehost the on-premises .NET application to an AWS Elastic Beanstalk Multi-AZ environment which runs in multiple Availability Zones.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10613" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Migrate the Oracle database to Amazon RDS for Oracle in a Multi-AZ deployment by using AWS Database Migration Service (AWS DMS).												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="4">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10613" value="5" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Provision and replatform the application to Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with Amazon EC2 worker nodes. Use the Windows Server Amazon Machine Image (AMI) and deploy the .NET application using to the ECS cluster via the Amazon ECS Anywhere service.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10613" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> 
Refactor the application to .NET Core and run it as a serverless container service using Amazon Elastic Kubernetes Service (Amazon EKS) with AWS Fargate.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">5. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="checkbox" name="question_45_10613" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Application Migration Service (AWS MGN) to migrate the on-premises Oracle database server to a new Amazon EC2 instance.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS Database Migration Service (AWS DMS)</strong> is a cloud service that makes it easy to migrate relational databases, data warehouses, NoSQL databases, and other types of data stores. You can use AWS DMS to migrate your data into the AWS Cloud or between combinations of cloud and on-premises setups.</p>
<p>With AWS DMS, you can perform one-time migrations, and you can replicate ongoing changes to keep sources and targets in sync. If you want to migrate to a different database engine, you can use the AWS Schema Conversion Tool (AWS SCT) to translate your database schema to the new platform. You then use AWS DMS to migrate the data.</p>
<p><strong>AWS Elastic Beanstalk</strong> reduces management complexity without restricting choice or control. You simply upload your application, and Elastic Beanstalk automatically handles the details of capacity provisioning, load balancing, scaling, and application health monitoring. Elastic Beanstalk supports applications developed in Go, Java, .NET, Node.js, PHP, Python, and Ruby. When you deploy your application, Elastic Beanstalk builds the selected supported platform version and provisions one or more AWS resources, such as Amazon EC2 instances, to run your application.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/saa_elastic_beanstalk_deploy.png" alt="" width="634" height="172"></p>
<p>AWS Elastic Beanstalk for .NET makes it easier to deploy, manage, and scale your ASP.NET web applications that use Amazon Web Services. Elastic Beanstalk for .NET is available to anyone who is developing or hosting a web application that uses IIS.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Migrate the Oracle database to Amazon RDS for Oracle in a Multi-AZ deployment by using AWS Database Migration Service (AWS DMS)</strong></span> is&nbsp;correct. AWS DMS can help migrate on-premises databases to the AWS Cloud.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Rehost the on-premises .NET application to an AWS Elastic Elastic Beanstalk Multi-AZ environment which runs in multiple Availability Zones</strong></span>&nbsp;is correct. AWS Beanstalk reduces the operational overhead by taking care of provisioning the needed resources for your application.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Refactor the application to .NET Core and run it as a serverless container service using Amazon Elastic Kubernetes Service (Amazon EKS) with AWS Fargate</strong></span> is incorrect. This will take significant changes to the application as you will refactor, or do a code change to, the codebase in order for it to become a serverless container application. Remember that the scenario explicitly mentioned that the migration process should minimize development changes. A better solution is to rehost the on-premises .NET application to an AWS Elastic Beanstalk Multi-AZ environment, which doesn’t require any code changes.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Application Migration Service (AWS MGN) to migrate the on-premises Oracle database server to a new Amazon EC2 instance</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect. Amazon RDS supports standard Oracle databases so it would be better to use AWS DMS for the database migration, not AWS MGN.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">&nbsp;Provision and replatform the application to Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with Amazon EC2 worker nodes. Use the Windows Server Amazon Machine Image (AMI) and deploy the .NET application using to the ECS cluster via the Amazon ECS Anywhere service</span>&nbsp;</strong>is incorrect. This may be possible but not recommended for this scenario because you will have to manage the underlying EC2 instances of your Amazon ECS cluster that will run the application. It would be better to use Elastic Beanstalk to take care of provisioning the resources for your .NET application. Keep in mind that doing a replatform-type migration like this one entails significant development changes, which is not suitable with the requirements given in the scenario.</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/create_deploy_NET.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/create_deploy_NET.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/Welcome.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/Welcome.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>45</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>45</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="220"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#bf2600">A government entity is conducting a population and housing census in the city. Each household information uploaded on their online portal is stored in encrypted files in Amazon S3. The government assigned its Solutions Architect to set compliance policies that verify data containing personally identifiable information (PII) in a manner that meets their compliance standards. They should also be alerted if there are potential policy violations with the privacy of their S3 buckets.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="705"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#bf2600">Which of the following should the Architect implement to satisfy this requirement?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10691" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10691" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up and configure Amazon Fraud Detector to send out alert notifications whenever a security violation is detected on their Amazon S3 data.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10691" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up and configure Amazon Polly to scan for usage patterns on Amazon S3 data												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10691" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up and configure Amazon Kendra to monitor malicious activity on their Amazon S3 data												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10691" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up and configure Amazon Macie to monitor their Amazon S3 data.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon Macie</strong> is an ML-powered security service that helps you prevent data loss by automatically discovering, classifying, and protecting sensitive data stored in Amazon S3. Amazon Macie uses machine learning to recognize sensitive data such as personally identifiable information (PII) or intellectual property, assigns a business value, and provides visibility into where this data is stored and how it is being used in your organization.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-macie-findings-samples.jpg" alt="" width="700" height="359"></p>
<p>Amazon Macie generates two categories of findings:&nbsp;policy findings&nbsp;and&nbsp;sensitive data findings. A&nbsp;policy finding&nbsp;is a detailed report of a potential policy violation or issue with the security or privacy of an Amazon S3 bucket. Macie generates these findings as part of its ongoing monitoring activities for your Amazon S3 data. A&nbsp;sensitive data finding&nbsp;is a detailed report of sensitive data in an S3 object. Macie generates these findings when it discovers sensitive data in S3 objects that you configure a sensitive data discovery job to analyze.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:<strong><em>&nbsp;</em><span style="color: #008000;">Set up and configure Amazon Macie to monitor their Amazon S3 data.</span></strong></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up and configure Amazon Polly to scan for usage patterns on Amazon S3 data</strong></span> is incorrect because Amazon Polly is simply a service that turns text into lifelike speech, allowing you to create applications that talk, and build entirely new categories of speech-enabled products. Polly can’t be used to scane usage patterns on your S3 data.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up and configure Amazon Kendra to monitor malicious activity on their Amazon S3 data </strong></span>is incorrect Amazon Kendra is just an enterprise search service that allows developers to add search capabilities to their applications. This enables their end users to discover information stored within the vast amount of content spread across their company, but not monitor malcious activity on their S3 buckets.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;"> Set up and configure Amazon Fraud Detector to send out alert notifications whenever a security violation is detected on their Amazon S3 data</span><em>&nbsp;</em></strong>is incorrect because the Amazon Fraud Detector is only a fully managed service for identifying potentially fraudulent activities and for catching more online fraud faster. It does not check any S3 data containing personally identifiable information (PII), unlike Amazon Macie.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/macie/latest/userguide/what-is-macie.html " target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/macie/latest/userguide/what-is-macie.html </a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/macie/faq/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/macie/faq/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/macie/index.html " target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/macie/index.html</a></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-macie/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-macie/</a></span></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10144,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29005}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>46</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>46</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="159">A Solutions Architect needs to set up a relational database and come up with a disaster recovery plan to mitigate multi-region failure. The solution requires a Recovery Point Objective (RPO) of 1 second and a Recovery Time Objective (RTO) of less than 1 minute.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="422">Which of the following AWS services can fulfill this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10144" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10144" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (Amazon QLDB)												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10144" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon RDS for PostgreSQL with cross-region read replicas												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10144" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon Timestream												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10144" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon Aurora Global Database												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon Aurora Global Database</strong> is designed for globally distributed applications, allowing a single Amazon Aurora database to span multiple AWS regions. It replicates your data with no impact on database performance, enables fast local reads with low latency in each region, and provides disaster recovery from region-wide outages.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/Aurora-PostgreSQL-Disaster-Recovery-A.png" alt="" width="549" height="197"></p>
<p>Aurora Global Database supports storage-based replication that has a latency of less than 1 second. If there is an unplanned outage, one of the secondary regions you assigned can be promoted to read and write capabilities in less than 1 minute. This feature is called Cross-Region Disaster Recovery. An RPO of 1 second and an RTO of less than 1 minute provide you a strong foundation for a global business continuity plan.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Amazon Aurora Global Database</strong></span>.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (Amazon QLDB)</strong></span> is incorrect because it is stated in the scenario that the Solutions Architect needs to create a relational database and not a ledger database. An Amazon Quantum Ledger Database (QLDB) is a fully managed ledger database that provides a transparent, immutable, and cryptographically verifiable transaction log. Moreover, QLDB cannot provide an RPO of 1 second and an RTO of less than 1 minute.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Multi-AZ Amazon RDS database with cross-region read replicas</strong></span> is incorrect because a Multi-AZ deployment is only applicable inside a single region and not in a multi-region setup. This database setup is not capable of providing an RPO of 1 second and an RTO of less than 1 minute. Moreover, the cross-region RDS Read Replica replication is not as fast as Amazon Aurora Global Databases.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Amazon Timestream</strong></span> is incorrect because this is a serverless time series database service that is commonly used for IoT and operational applications. The most suitable solution for this scenario is to use the Amazon Aurora Global Database since it can provide the required RPO and RTO.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/global-database/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/global-database/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-global-database.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/aurora-global-database.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:9942,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28893}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>47</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>47</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="167">A company hosted a web application in an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances. The IT manager is concerned about the over-provisioning of the resources that can cause higher operating costs. A Solutions Architect has been instructed to create a cost-effective solution without affecting the performance of the application.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="490">Which dynamic scaling policy should be used to satisfy this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="9942" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9942" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use suspend and resume scaling.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9942" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use scheduled scaling.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9942" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use simple scaling.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9942" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use target tracking scaling.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>An <strong>Auto Scaling group</strong> contains a collection of Amazon EC2 instances that are treated as a logical grouping for the purposes of automatic scaling and management. An Auto Scaling group also enables you to use Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling features such as health check replacements and scaling policies. Both maintaining the number of instances in an Auto Scaling group and automatic scaling are the core functionality of the Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling service. The size of an Auto Scaling group depends on the number of instances that you set as the desired capacity. You can adjust its size to meet demand, either manually or by using automatic scaling.</p>
<p>Step scaling policies and simple scaling policies are two of the dynamic scaling options available for you to use. Both require you to create CloudWatch alarms for the scaling policies. Both require you to specify the high and low thresholds for the alarms. Both require you to define whether to add or remove instances, and how many, or set the group to an exact size. The main difference between the policy types is the step adjustments that you get with step scaling policies. When step adjustments are applied, and they increase or decrease the current capacity of your Auto Scaling group, the adjustments vary based on the size of the alarm breach.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/as-basic-diagram.png" width="700" height="506"></p>
<p>The primary issue with simple scaling is that after a scaling activity is started, the policy must wait for the scaling activity or health check replacement to complete and the cooldown period to expire before responding to additional alarms. Cooldown periods help to prevent the initiation of additional scaling activities before the effects of previous activities are visible.</p>
<p>With a target tracking scaling policy, you can increase or decrease the current capacity of the group based on a target value for a specific metric. This policy will help resolve the over-provisioning of your resources. The scaling policy adds or removes capacity as required to keep the metric at, or close to, the specified target value. In addition to keeping the metric close to the target value, a target tracking scaling policy also adjusts to changes in the metric due to a changing load pattern.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:<span style="color: #008000;"><strong> Use target tracking scaling.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:<strong><span style="color: #ff6600;"> Use simple scaling</span> </strong>is incorrect because you need to wait for the cooldown period to complete before initiating additional scaling activities. Target tracking or step scaling policies can trigger a scaling activity immediately without waiting for the cooldown period to expire.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Use scheduled scaling</strong> </span>is incorrect because this policy is mainly used for predictable traffic patterns. You need to use the target tracking scaling policy to optimize the cost of your infrastructure without affecting the performance.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Use suspend and resume scaling</strong> </span>is incorrect because this type is used to temporarily pause scaling activities triggered by your scaling policies and scheduled actions.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-scaling-target-tracking.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-scaling-target-tracking.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/AutoScalingGroup.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/AutoScalingGroup.html</a></p>

</p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:9497,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28913}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>48</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>48</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An AI-powered Forex trading application consumes thousands of data sets to train its machine learning model. The application’s workload requires a high-performance, parallel hot storage to process the training datasets concurrently. It also needs cost-effective cold storage to archive those datasets that yield low profit.</p>
<p>Which of the following Amazon storage services should the developer use?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="9497" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9497" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon FSx For Lustre and Amazon EBS Provisioned IOPS SSD (io1) volumes for hot and cold storage respectively.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9497" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon Elastic File System and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9497" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon FSx For Windows File Server and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9497" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon FSx For Lustre and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Hot storage</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> refers to the storage that keeps frequently accessed data (hot data). </span><strong>Warm storage</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> refers to the storage that keeps less frequently accessed data (warm data). </span><strong>Cold storage</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> refers to the storage that keeps rarely accessed data (cold data). In terms of pricing, the colder the data, </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">the cheaper it is to store, and the costlier it is to access when needed.</span></p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-storage-services.png" alt="" width="700" height="484"></p>
<p><strong>Amazon FSx For Lustre </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">is a high-performance file system for fast processing of workloads. Lustre is a popular open-source</span><strong> parallel file system</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> which stores data across multiple network file servers to maximize performance and reduce bottlenecks.</span></p>
<p><strong>Amazon FSx for Windows File Server </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">is a fully managed Microsoft Windows file system with full support for the SMB protocol, Windows NTFS, Microsoft Active Directory (AD) Integration.</span></p>
<p><strong>Amazon Elastic File System</strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"> is a fully-managed file storage service that makes it easy to set up and scale file storage in the Amazon Cloud.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong>Amazon S3 is </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">an object storage service that offers industry-leading scalability, data availability, security, and performance. S3 offers different storage tiers for different use cases (frequently accessed data, infrequently accessed data, and rarely accessed data).</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-weight: 400;">The question has two requirements:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="font-weight: 400;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">High-performance, parallel hot storage to process the training datasets concurrently.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Cost-effective cold storage to keep the archived datasets that are accessed infrequently</span></li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this case, we can use </span><strong>Amazon FSx For Lustre </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">for the first requirement, as it provides a high-performance, parallel file system for hot data. On the second requirement, we can use Amazon S3 for storing cold data. Amazon S3 supports a cold storage system via Amazon S3 Glacier / Glacier Deep Archive.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Hence, the correct answer is: </span><span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use Amazon FSx For Lustre and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively.</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using Amazon FSx For Lustre and Amazon EBS Provisioned IOPS SSD (io1) volumes for hot and cold storage respectively</strong></span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> is incorrect because the Provisioned IOPS SSD (io1) volumes are designed for storing hot data (data that are frequently accessed) used in I/O-intensive workloads. EBS has a storage option called “Cold HDD,” but due to its price, it is not ideal for data archiving. EBS Cold HDD is much more expensive than Amazon S3 Glacier / Glacier Deep Archive and is often utilized in applications where sequential cold data is read less frequently.</span></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using Amazon Elastic File System and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively </strong></span><span style="font-weight: 400;">is incorrect. Although EFS supports concurrent access to data, it does not have the high-performance ability that is required for machine learning workloads.</span></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using Amazon FSx For Windows File Server and Amazon S3 for hot and cold storage respectively</strong></span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> is incorrect because Amazon FSx For Windows File Server does not have a parallel file system, unlike Lustre.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/</span></a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/whitepapers/latest/cost-optimization-storage-optimization/aws-storage-services.html</span></a></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/fsx/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/startups/picking-the-right-data-store-for-your-workload/</span></a></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-fsx/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-fsx/</a></span></p>
</p>
								</div>
