									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10141,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29014}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>49</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>49</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="159">A company needs to deploy at least 2 EC2 instances to support the normal workloads of its application and automatically scale up to 6 EC2 instances to handle the peak load. The architecture must be highly available and fault-tolerant as it is processing mission-critical workloads.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="442">As the Solutions Architect of the company, what should you do to meet the above requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10141" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10141" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 4 and the maximum capacity to 6. Deploy 2 instances in Availability Zone A and another 2 instances in Availability Zone B.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10141" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 6. Deploy 4 instances in Availability Zone A.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10141" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 4. Deploy 2 instances in Availability Zone A and 2 instances in Availability Zone B.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10141" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 6. Use 2 Availability Zones and deploy 1 instance for each AZ.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling</strong> helps ensure that you have the correct number of Amazon EC2 instances available to handle the load for your application. You create collections of EC2 instances, called Auto Scaling groups. You can specify the minimum number of instances in each Auto Scaling group, and Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling ensures that your group never goes below this size. You can also specify the maximum number of instances in each Auto Scaling group, and Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling ensures that your group never goes above this size.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/images/as-basic-diagram.png" alt=" An illustration of a basic Auto Scaling group. "></p>
<p>To achieve highly available and fault-tolerant architecture for your applications, you must deploy all your instances in different Availability Zones. This will help you isolate your resources if an outage occurs. Take note that to achieve fault tolerance, you need to have redundant resources in place to avoid any system degradation in the event of a server fault or an Availability Zone outage. Having a fault-tolerant architecture entails an extra cost in running additional resources than what is usually needed. This is to ensure that the mission-critical workloads are processed.</p>
<p>Since the scenario requires at least 2 instances to handle regular traffic, you should have 2 instances running all the time even if an AZ outage occurred. You can use an Auto Scaling Group to automatically scale your compute resources across two or more Availability Zones. You have to specify the minimum capacity to 4 instances and the maximum capacity to 6 instances. If each AZ has 2 instances running, even if an AZ fails, your system will still run a minimum of 2 instances.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is:<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>&nbsp;Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 4 and the maximum capacity to 6. Deploy 2 instances in Availability Zone A and another 2 instances in Availability Zone B.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 6. Deploy 4 instances in Availability Zone A</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because the instances are only deployed in a single Availability Zone. It cannot protect your applications and data from datacenter or AZ failures.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 6. Use 2 Availability Zones and deploy 1 instance for each AZ</strong></span> is incorrect. It is required to have 2 instances running all the time. If an AZ outage happened, ASG will launch a new instance on the unaffected AZ. This provisioning does not happen instantly, which means that for a certain period of time, there will only be 1 running instance left.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances and set the minimum capacity to 2 and the maximum capacity to 4. Deploy 2 instances in Availability Zone A and 2 instances in Availability Zone B</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect. Although this fulfills the requirement of at least 2 EC2 instances and high availability, the maximum capacity setting is wrong. It should be set to 6 to properly handle the peak load. If an AZ outage occurs and the system is at its peak load, the number of running instances in this setup will only be 4 instead of 6 and this will affect the performance of your application.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/what-is-amazon-ec2-auto-scaling.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/what-is-amazon-ec2-auto-scaling.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/documentdb/latest/developerguide/regions-and-azs.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/documentdb/latest/developerguide/regions-and-azs.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/aws-auto-scaling/</a></p>
</p>
								</div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:9674,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29025}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>50</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>50</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A company has a hybrid cloud architecture that connects their on-premises data center and cloud infrastructure in AWS. They require a durable storage backup for their corporate documents stored on-premises and a local cache that provides low latency access to their recently accessed data to reduce data egress charges. The documents must be stored to and retrieved from AWS via the Server Message Block (SMB) protocol. These files must immediately be accessible within minutes for six months and archived for another decade to meet the data compliance.</p>
<p>Which of the following is the best and most cost-effective approach to implement in this scenario?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="9674" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9674" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Snowmobile to migrate all of the files from the on-premises network. Upload the documents to an S3 bucket and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for archival.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9674" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Establish a Direct Connect connection to integrate your on-premises network to your VPC. Upload the documents on Amazon EBS Volumes and use a lifecycle policy to automatically move the EBS snapshots to an S3 bucket, and then later to Glacier for archival.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9674" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch a new tape gateway that connects to your on-premises data center using AWS Storage Gateway. Upload the documents to the tape gateway and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for archival.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9674" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch a new file gateway that connects to your on-premises data center using AWS Storage Gateway. Upload the documents to the file gateway and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for data archival.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>A file gateway supports a file interface into Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3) and combines a service and a virtual software appliance. By using this combination, you can store and retrieve objects in Amazon S3 using industry-standard file protocols such as Network File System (NFS) and Server Message Block (SMB). The software appliance, or gateway, is deployed into your on-premises environment as a virtual machine (VM) running on VMware ESXi, Microsoft Hyper-V, or Linux Kernel-based Virtual Machine (KVM) hypervisor.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/file-gateway.jpg" alt="" width="700" height="191"></p>
<p>The gateway provides access to objects in S3 as files or file share mount points. With a file gateway, you can do the following:</p>
<div>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You can store and retrieve files directly using the NFS version 3 or 4.1 protocol.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You can store and retrieve files directly using the SMB file system version, 2 and 3 protocol.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You can access your data directly in Amazon S3 from any AWS Cloud application or service.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– You can manage your Amazon S3 data using lifecycle policies, cross-region replication, and versioning. You can think of a file gateway as a file system mount on S3.</p>
</div>
<p>AWS Storage Gateway supports the Amazon S3 Standard, Amazon S3 Standard-Infrequent Access, Amazon S3 One Zone-Infrequent Access and Amazon Glacier storage classes. When you create or update a file share, you have the option to select a storage class for your objects. You can either choose the Amazon S3 Standard or any of the infrequent access storage classes such as S3 Standard IA or S3 One Zone IA. Objects stored in any of these storage classes can be transitioned to Amazon Glacier using a Lifecycle Policy.</p>
<p>Although you can write objects directly from a file share to the S3-Standard-IA or S3-One Zone-IA storage class, it is recommended that you use a Lifecycle Policy to transition your objects rather than write directly from the file share, especially if you’re expecting to update or delete the object within 30 days of archiving it.</p>
<p>Therefore, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Launch a new file gateway that connects to your on-premises data center using AWS Storage Gateway. Upload the documents to the file gateway and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for data archival.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launch a new tape gateway that connects to your on-premises data center using AWS Storage Gateway. Upload the documents to the tape gateway and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for archival</strong></span> is incorrect because although tape gateways provide cost-effective and durable archive backup data in Amazon Glacier, it does not meet the criteria of being retrievable immediately within minutes. It also doesn’t maintain a local cache that provides low latency access to the recently accessed data and reduce data egress charges. Thus,&nbsp;it is still better to set up a file gateway instead.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Establish a Direct Connect connection to integrate your on-premises network to your VPC. Upload the documents on Amazon EBS Volumes and use a lifecycle policy to automatically move the EBS snapshots to an S3 bucket, and then later to Glacier for archival</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because EBS Volumes are not as durable compared with S3 and it would be more cost-efficient if you directly store the documents to an S3 bucket.&nbsp;An alternative solution is to use AWS Direct Connect with AWS Storage Gateway to create a connection for high-throughput workload needs, providing a dedicated network connection between your on-premises file gateway and AWS. But this solution is using EBS, hence, this option is still wrong.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Snowmobile to migrate all of the files from the on-premises network. Upload the documents to an S3 bucket and set up a lifecycle policy to move the data into Glacier for archival</strong></span> is incorrect because Snowmobile is mainly used to migrate the entire data of an on-premises data center to AWS. This is not a suitable approach as the company still has a hybrid cloud architecture which means that they will still use their on-premises data center along with their AWS cloud infrastructure.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lifecycle-mgmt.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/userguide/StorageGatewayConcepts.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/userguide/StorageGatewayConcepts.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10080,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28921}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>51</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>51</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An online cryptocurrency exchange platform is hosted in AWS which uses ECS Cluster and RDS in Multi-AZ Deployments configuration. The application is heavily using the RDS instance to process complex read and write database operations. To maintain the reliability, availability, and performance of your systems, you have to closely monitor how the different processes or threads on a DB instance use the CPU, including the percentage of the CPU bandwidth and total memory consumed by each process.</p>
<p>Which of the following is the most suitable solution to properly monitor your database?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10080" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10080" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Check the <code>CPU%</code> and <code>MEM%</code> metrics which are readily available in the Amazon RDS console that shows the percentage of the CPU bandwidth and total memory consumed by each database process of your RDS instance.</span>												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10080" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable Enhanced Monitoring in RDS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10080" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a script that collects and publishes custom metrics to CloudWatch, which tracks the real-time CPU Utilization of the RDS instance, and then set up a custom CloudWatch dashboard to view the metrics.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10080" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use Amazon CloudWatch to monitor the CPU Utilization of your database.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Amazon RDS provides metrics in real time for the operating system (OS) that your DB instance runs on. You can view the metrics for your DB instance using the console, or consume the Enhanced Monitoring JSON output from CloudWatch Logs in a monitoring system of your choice. By default, Enhanced Monitoring metrics are stored in the CloudWatch Logs for 30 days. To modify the amount of time the metrics are stored in the CloudWatch Logs, change the retention for the&nbsp;<code class="code">RDSOSMetrics</code>&nbsp;log group in the CloudWatch console.</p>
<p>Take note that&nbsp;there are certain differences between CloudWatch and Enhanced Monitoring Metrics.&nbsp; CloudWatch gathers metrics about CPU utilization from the hypervisor for a DB instance, and Enhanced Monitoring gathers its metrics from an agent on the instance. As a result, you might find differences between the measurements, because the hypervisor layer performs a small amount of work. Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>enabling Enhanced Monitoring in RDS</strong></span> is the correct answer in this specific scenario.</p>
<p>The differences can be greater if your DB instances use smaller instance classes, because then there are likely more virtual machines (VMs) that are managed by the hypervisor layer on a single physical instance. Enhanced Monitoring metrics are useful when you want to see how different processes or threads on a DB instance use the CPU.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/metrics2.png" alt="" width="722" height="389"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using Amazon CloudWatch to monitor the CPU Utilization of your database</strong></span> is incorrect. Although you can use this to monitor the CPU Utilization of your database instance, it does not provide the percentage of the CPU bandwidth and total memory consumed by each database process in your RDS instance. Take note that CloudWatch gathers metrics about CPU utilization from the hypervisor for a DB instance while RDS Enhanced Monitoring gathers its metrics from an agent on the instance.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create a script that collects and publishes custom metrics to CloudWatch, which tracks the real-time CPU Utilization of the RDS instance and then set up a custom CloudWatch dashboard to view the metrics</strong></span> is incorrect. Although you can use Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch dashboard to monitor the CPU Utilization of the database instance, using CloudWatch alone is still not enough to get the specific percentage of the CPU bandwidth and total memory consumed by each database processes. The data provided by CloudWatch is not as detailed as compared with the Enhanced Monitoring feature in RDS. Take note as well that you do not have direct access to the instances/servers of your RDS database instance, unlike with your EC2 instances where you can install a CloudWatch agent or a custom script to get CPU and memory utilization of your instance.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Check the <code>CPU%</code> and <code>MEM%</code> metrics which are readily available in the Amazon RDS console that shows the percentage of the CPU bandwidth and total memory consumed by each database process of your RDS instance</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;the CPU% and MEM% metrics are not readily available in the Amazon RDS console, which is contrary to what is being stated in this option.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">
</p><p><strong>References:&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/USER_Monitoring.OS.html#USER_Monitoring.OS.CloudWatchLogs" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/USER_Monitoring.OS.html#USER_Monitoring.OS.CloudWatchLogs</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/MonitoringOverview.html#monitoring-cloudwatch" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/MonitoringOverview.html#monitoring-cloudwatch</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Check out this&nbsp;Amazon CloudWatch Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-cloudwatch/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-cloudwatch/</a></p>

</p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10075,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28909}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>52</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>52</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="195">A company is using Amazon S3 to store frequently accessed data. When an object is created or deleted, the S3 bucket will send an event notification to the Amazon SQS queue. A solutions architect needs to create a solution that will notify the development and operations team about the created or deleted objects.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="509">Which of the following would satisfy this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10075" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10075" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Amazon SNS topic and configure two Amazon SQS queues to subscribe to the topic. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send notifications to Amazon SNS and update the bucket to use the new SNS topic.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10075" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an Amazon SNS topic and configure two Amazon SQS queues to poll the SNS topic. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send notifications to Amazon SNS and update the bucket to use the new SNS topic.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10075" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a new Amazon SNS FIFO topic for the other team. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send the notification to the second SNS topic.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10075" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up another Amazon SQS queue for the other team. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send a notification to the second SQS queue.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>The <strong>Amazon S3</strong> notification feature enables you to receive notifications when certain events happen in your bucket. To enable notifications, you must first add a notification configuration that identifies the events you want Amazon S3 to publish and the destinations where you want Amazon S3 to send the notifications. You store this configuration in the notification subresource that is associated with a bucket.</p>
<p>Amazon S3 supports the following destinations where it can publish events:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Amazon Simple Notification Service (Amazon SNS) topic</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) queue</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– AWS Lambda</p>
<p>In Amazon SNS, the&nbsp;<em>fanout</em>&nbsp;scenario is when a message published to an SNS topic is replicated and pushed to multiple endpoints, such as Amazon SQS queues, HTTP(S) endpoints, and Lambda functions. This allows for parallel asynchronous processing.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/event_driven_sns_compute_slide05.png" width="700" height="237"></p>
<p>For example, you can develop an application that publishes a message to an SNS topic whenever an order is placed for a product. Then, SQS queues that are subscribed to the SNS topic receive identical notifications for the new order. An Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (Amazon EC2) server instance attached to one of the SQS queues can handle the processing or fulfillment of the order. And you can attach another Amazon EC2 server instance to a data warehouse for analysis of all orders received.</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 [&quot;layoutSection&quot;,null,&quot;layoutColumn&quot;,null]">Based on the given scenario, the existing setup sends the event notification to an SQS queue. Since you need to send the notification to the development and operations team, you can use a combination of Amazon SNS and SQS. By using the message fanout pattern, you can create a topic and use two Amazon SQS queues to subscribe to the topic. If Amazon SNS receives an event notification, it will publish the message to both subscribers.</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 [&quot;layoutSection&quot;,null,&quot;layoutColumn&quot;,null]">Take note that Amazon S3 event notifications are designed to be delivered at least once and to one destination only. You cannot attach two or more SNS topics or SQS queues for S3 event notification. Therefore, you must send the event notification to Amazon SNS.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:<span style="color: #008000;"><strong> Create an Amazon SNS topic and configure two Amazon SQS queues to subscribe to the topic. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send notifications to Amazon SNS and update the bucket to use the new SNS topic.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Set up another Amazon SQS queue for the other team. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send a notification to the second SQS queue&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect because you can only add 1 SQS or SNS at a time for Amazon S3 events notification. If you need to send the events to multiple subscribers, you should implement a message fanout pattern with Amazon SNS and Amazon SQS.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong>&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;">Create a new Amazon SNS FIFO topic for the other team. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send the notification to the second SNS topic&nbsp;</span></strong>is incorrect. Just as mentioned in the previous option, you can only add 1 SQS or SNS at a time for Amazon S3 events notification. In addition, neither Amazon SNS FIFO topic nor Amazon SQS FIFO queue is warranted in this scenario. Both of them can be used together to provide strict message ordering and message deduplication. The FIFO capabilities of each of these services work together to act as a fully managed service to integrate distributed applications that require data consistency in near-real-time.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong>&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;">Set up an Amazon SNS topic and configure two Amazon SQS queues to poll the SNS topic. Grant Amazon S3 permission to send notifications to Amazon SNS and update the bucket to use the new SNS topic&nbsp;</span></strong>is incorrect because you can’t poll Amazon SNS. Instead of configuring queues to poll Amazon SNS, you should configure each Amazon SQS queue to subscribe to the SNS topic.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/NotificationHowTo.html#notification-how-to-overview" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/NotificationHowTo.html#notification-how-to-overview</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/sns/latest/dg/welcome.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/sns/latest/dg/welcome.html</a></p>

							Question <span>53</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>53</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="173">A Solutions Architect designed a serverless architecture that allows AWS Lambda to access an Amazon DynamoDB table named tutorialsdojo in the US East (N. Virginia) region. The IAM policy attached to a Lambda function allows it to put and delete items in the table. The policy must be updated to only allow two operations in the tutorialsdojo table and prevent other DynamoDB tables from being modified.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="577">Which of the following IAM policies fulfill this requirement and follows the principle of granting the least privilege?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10699" data-type="single">

													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10699" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span><pre>{<br>
 "Version": "2012-10-17",<br>

   }<br>
 ]<br>

												<label>

												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10699" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span><pre>{<br>
 "Version": "2012-10-17",<br>
 "Statement": [<br>
   {<br>
     "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy1",<br>
     "Effect": "Allow",<br>
     "Action": [<br>
       "dynamodb:PutItem",<br>
       "dynamodb:DeleteItem"<br>
      ],<br>
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/tutorialsdojo"<br>
   },<br>
<br>
   {<br>
     "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy2",<br>
     "Effect": "Deny",<br>
     "Action": "dynamodb:*",<br>
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/*"<br>
   }<br>
 ]<br>
}<br>
</pre></span>												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Every AWS resource is owned by an AWS account, and permissions to create or access a resource are governed by permissions policies. An account administrator can attach permissions policies to IAM identities (that is, users, groups, and roles), and some services (such as AWS Lambda) also support attaching permissions policies to resources.</p>
<p>In DynamoDB, the primary resources are tables. DynamoDB also supports additional resource types, indexes, and streams. However, you can create indexes and streams only in the context of an existing DynamoDB table. These are referred to as subresources. These resources and subresources have unique Amazon Resource Names (ARNs) associated with them.</p>
<p>For example, an AWS Account (123456789012) has a DynamoDB table named <em>Books</em> in the US East (N. Virginia) (us-east-1) region. The ARN of the <em>Books</em> table would be:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><code>arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:123456789012:table/Books</code></p>
<p>A policy is an entity that, when attached to an identity or resource, defines their permissions. By using an IAM policy and role to control access, it will grant a Lambda function access to a DynamoDB table.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-7139 size-full" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Screenshot of the review page of the role-creation process" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/AR7_0118.png" alt="Screenshot of the review page of the role-creation process" width="542" height="327"></p>
<p>It is stated in the scenario that a Lambda function will be used to modify the DynamoDB table named <strong>tutorialsdojo</strong>. Since you only need to access one table, you will need to indicate that table in the resource element of the IAM policy. Also, you must specify the effect and action elements that will be generated in the policy.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is:</p>
<pre><strong><span style="color: #008000;">{
 "Version": "2012-10-17",
 "Statement": [
   {
     "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy",
     "Effect": "Allow",
     "Action": [
       "dynamodb:PutItem",
       "dynamodb:DeleteItem"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:120618981206:table/tutorialsdojo"
   }
 ]
}
</span></strong></pre>
<p>The IAM policy below is incorrect because the scenario only requires you to allow the permissions in the <em>tutorialsdojo</em> table. Having a wildcard:&nbsp;<strong>table/*</strong> in this policy would allow the Lambda function to modify all the DynamoDB tables in your account.</p>
<pre><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">{
 {
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "dynamodb:PutItem",
        "dynamodb:DeleteItem"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:120618981206:table/*"
    }
  ]
}
</span></strong></pre>
<p>The IAM policy below is incorrect. The first statement is correctly allowing PUT and DELETE actions to the <em>tutorialsdojo</em> DynamoDB table. However, the second statement counteracts the first one as it allows all DynamoDB actions in the <em>tutorialsdojo</em> table.</p>
<pre><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy1",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [ "dynamodb:PutItem", "dynamodb:DeleteItem" ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/tutorialsdojo"
    },
    {
      "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy2",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": "dynamodb:*",
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/tutorialsdojo"
    }
  ]
}
</span></strong></pre>
<p>The IAM policy below is incorrect.&nbsp;Just like the previous option, the first statement of this policy is correctly allowing PUT and DELETE actions to the <em>tutorialsdojo</em> DynamoDB table. However, the second statement counteracts the first one as it denies all DynamoDB actions. Therefore, this policy will not allow any actions on all DynamoDB tables of the AWS account.</p>
<pre><strong><span style="color: #ff6600;">
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy1",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "dynamodb:PutItem",
        "dynamodb:DeleteItem"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/tutorialsdojo"
    },
    {
      "Sid": "TutorialsdojoTablePolicy2",
      "Effect": "Deny",
      "Action": "dynamodb:*",
      "Resource": "arn:aws:dynamodb:us-east-1:1206189812061898:table/*"
    }
  ]
}
</span></strong></pre>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/using-identity-based-policies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/using-identity-based-policies.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/cognito/latest/developerguide/what-is-amazon-cognito.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/reference_policies_examples_lambda-access-dynamodb.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10087,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28944}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>54</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>54</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A popular social network is hosted in AWS and is using a DynamoDB table as its database. There is a requirement to implement a ‘follow’ feature where users can subscribe to certain updates made by a particular user and be notified via email.</p>
<p>Which of the following is the most suitable solution that you should implement to meet the requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10087" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10087" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Using the Kinesis Client Library (KCL), write an application that leverages on DynamoDB Streams Kinesis Adapter that will fetch data from the DynamoDB Streams endpoint. When there are updates made by a particular user, notify the subscribers via email using SNS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10087" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a Lambda function that uses DynamoDB Streams Kinesis Adapter which will fetch data from the DynamoDB Streams endpoint. Set up an SNS Topic that will notify the subscribers via email when there is an update made by a particular user.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10087" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a DAX cluster to access the source DynamoDB table. Create a new DynamoDB trigger and a Lambda function. For every update made in the user data, the trigger will send data to the Lambda function which will then notify the subscribers via email using SNS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10087" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable DynamoDB Stream and create an AWS Lambda trigger, as well as the IAM role which contains all of the permissions that the Lambda function will need at runtime. The data from the stream record will be processed by the Lambda function which will then publish a message to SNS Topic that will notify the subscribers via email.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>A&nbsp;<strong>DynamoDB stream</strong>&nbsp;is an ordered flow of information about changes to items in an Amazon DynamoDB table. When you enable a stream on a table, DynamoDB captures information about every modification to data items in the table.</p>
<p>Whenever an application creates, updates, or deletes items in the table, DynamoDB Streams writes a stream record with the primary key attribute(s) of the items that were modified. A&nbsp;<em>stream record&nbsp;</em>contains information about a data modification to a single item in a DynamoDB table. You can configure the stream so that the stream records capture additional information, such as the “before” and “after” images of modified items.</p>
<p>Amazon DynamoDB is integrated with AWS Lambda so that you can create&nbsp;<em>triggers</em>—pieces of code that automatically respond to events in DynamoDB Streams. With triggers, you can build applications that react to data modifications in DynamoDB tables.</p>
<p>If you enable DynamoDB Streams on a table, you can associate the stream ARN with a Lambda function that you write. Immediately after an item in the table is modified, a new record appears in the table’s stream. AWS Lambda polls the stream and invokes your Lambda function synchronously when it detects new stream records. The Lambda function can perform any actions you specify, such as sending a notification or initiating a workflow.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer in this scenario is the option that says: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Enable DynamoDB Stream and create an AWS Lambda trigger, as well as the IAM role which contains all of the permissions that the Lambda function will need at runtime. The data from the stream record will be processed by the Lambda function which will then publish a message to SNS Topic that will notify the subscribers via email</strong></span>.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/StreamsAndTriggers.png" alt="" width="684" height="370"></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using the Kinesis Client Library (KCL), write an application that leverages on DynamoDB Streams Kinesis Adapter that will fetch data from the DynamoDB Streams endpoint. When there are updates made by a particular user, notify the subscribers via email using SNS</strong></span> is incorrect. Although this is a valid solution, it is missing a vital step which is to enable DynamoDB Streams.&nbsp;With the DynamoDB Streams Kinesis Adapter in place, you can begin developing applications via the KCL interface, with the API calls seamlessly directed at the DynamoDB Streams endpoint. Remember that the DynamoDB Stream feature is not enabled by default.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create a Lambda function that uses DynamoDB Streams Kinesis Adapter which will fetch data from the DynamoDB Streams endpoint. Set up an SNS Topic that will notify the subscribers via email when there is an update made by a particular user</strong></span> is incorrect because just like in the above, you have to manually enable DynamoDB Streams first before you can use its endpoint.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up a DAX cluster to access the source DynamoDB table. Create a new DynamoDB trigger and a Lambda function. For every update made in the user data, the trigger will send data to the Lambda function which will then notify the subscribers via email using SNS</strong></span> is incorrect because the DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) feature is primarily used to significantly improve the in-memory read performance of your database, and not to capture the time-ordered sequence of item-level modifications. You should use&nbsp;DynamoDB Streams in this scenario instead.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/Streams.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/Streams.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/Streams.Lambda.Tutorial.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/Streams.Lambda.Tutorial.html</a></p>

													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A company needs to design an online analytics application that uses Redshift Cluster for its data warehouse. Which of the following services allows them to monitor all API calls in Redshift instance and can also provide secured data for auditing and compliance purposes?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10675" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10675" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon CloudWatch												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10675" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> AWS CloudTrail												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10675" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> AWS X-Ray												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10675" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon Redshift Spectrum												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS CloudTrail</strong> is a service that enables governance, compliance, operational auditing, and risk auditing of your AWS account. With CloudTrail, you can log, continuously monitor, and retain account activity related to actions across your AWS infrastructure. By default, CloudTrail is enabled on your AWS account when you create it. When activity occurs in your AWS account, that activity is recorded in a CloudTrail event. You can easily view recent events in the CloudTrail console by going to Event history.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/cloudtrail_revised_flow_2.png" width="1058" height="769"></p>
<p>CloudTrail provides event history of your AWS account activity, including actions taken through the AWS Management Console, AWS SDKs, command line tools,&nbsp;API calls,&nbsp;and other AWS services. This event history simplifies security analysis, resource change tracking, and troubleshooting.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>AWS CloudTrail.</strong></span></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Amazon CloudWatch</strong></span> is incorrect. Although this is also a monitoring service, it cannot track the API calls to your AWS resources.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>AWS X-Ray</strong></span> is incorrect because this is not a suitable&nbsp;service to use to track each API call to your AWS resources. It&nbsp;just helps you debug and analyze your microservices applications with request tracing so you can find the root cause of issues and performance.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Amazon Redshift Spectrum</strong></span> is incorrect because this is not a monitoring service but rather a feature of Amazon Redshift that enables you to query and analyze all of your data in Amazon S3 using the open data formats you already use, with no data loading or transformations needed.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>

							Question <span>56</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>56</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>The company that you are working for has a highly available architecture consisting of an elastic load balancer and several EC2 instances configured with auto-scaling in three Availability Zones. You want to monitor your EC2 instances based on a particular metric, which is not readily available in CloudWatch.</p>
<p>Which of the following is a custom metric in CloudWatch which you have to manually set up?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10073" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10073" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> CPU Utilization of an EC2 instance												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10073" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Disk Reads activity of an EC2 instance												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10073" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Network packets out of an EC2 instance												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10073" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Memory Utilization of an EC2 instance												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>CloudWatch has available Amazon EC2 Metrics for you to use for monitoring. CPU Utilization identifies the processing power required to run an application upon a selected instance. Network Utilization identifies the volume of incoming and outgoing network traffic to a single instance. Disk Reads metric is used to determine the volume of the data the application reads from the hard disk of the instance. This can be used to determine the speed of the application. However, there are certain metrics that are not readily available in CloudWatch such as memory utilization, disk space utilization, and many others which can be collected by setting up a custom metric.</p>
<p>You need to prepare a custom metric using CloudWatch Monitoring Scripts which is written in Perl.&nbsp;You can also install CloudWatch Agent to collect more system-level metrics from Amazon EC2 instances. Here’s the list of custom metrics that you can set up:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Memory utilization<br>
– Disk swap utilization<br>
– Disk space utilization<br>
– Page file utilization<br>
– Log collection</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-02-13_00-48-03-503799cd694a657201456b3add758b53.png" width="350" height="411"></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>CPU Utilization of an EC2 instance</strong></span>, <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Disk Reads activity of an EC2 instance</strong></span>, and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Network packets out of an EC2 instance</strong></span> are all incorrect because these metrics are readily available in CloudWatch by default.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/monitoring_ec2.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/monitoring_ec2.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/mon-scripts.html#using_put_script" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/mon-scripts.html#using_put_script</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>57</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>57</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Secure Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="206"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company has 3 DevOps engineers that are handling its software development and infrastructure management processes. One of the engineers accidentally deleted a file hosted in Amazon S3 which has caused disruption of service. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="434"><span data-renderer-mark="true">What can the DevOps engineers do to prevent this from happening again?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10645" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10645" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an IAM bucket policy that disables delete operation.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10645" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable S3 Versioning and Multi-Factor Authentication Delete on the bucket.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10645" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use S3 Infrequently Accessed storage to store the data.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10645" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up a signed URL for all users.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p style="text-align: left;">To avoid accidental deletion in Amazon S3 bucket, you can:</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp; &nbsp; – Enable Versioning</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp; &nbsp; – Enable MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication) Delete</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Versioning is a means of keeping multiple variants of an object in the same bucket. You can use versioning to preserve, retrieve, and restore every version of every object stored in your Amazon S3 bucket. With versioning, you can easily recover from both unintended user actions and application failures.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">If the MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication) Delete is enabled, it requires additional authentication for either of the following operations:</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp; &nbsp; – Change the versioning state of your bucket</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp; &nbsp; – Permanently delete an object version</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using S3 Infrequently Accessed storage to store the data</strong></span> is incorrect. Switching your storage class to S3 Infrequent Access won’t help mitigate accidental deletions.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Setting up a signed URL for all users</strong></span> is incorrect. Signed URLs give you more control over access to your content, so this feature deals more on accessing rather than deletion.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Creating an IAM bucket policy that disables delete operation</strong></span> is incorrect. If you create a bucket policy preventing deletion, other users won’t be able to delete objects that should be deleted. You only want to prevent accidental deletion, not disable the action itself.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>Reference:</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Versioning.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">http://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Versioning.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>Check out this Amazon S3 Cheat Sheet:</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">https://tutorialsdojo.com/amazon-s3/</span></a></p>
</p>
								</div>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10441,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:29003}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>58</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>58</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="197">A company wishes to query data that resides in multiple AWS accounts from a central data lake. Each account has its own Amazon S3 bucket that stores data unique to its business function. Users from different accounts must be granted access to the data lake based on their roles.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="477">Which solution will minimize overhead and costs while meeting the required access patterns?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10441" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10441" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a scheduled Lambda function for transferring data from multiple accounts to the S3 buckets of a central account												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10441" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Kinesis Firehose to consolidate data from multiple accounts into a single account.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10441" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Control Tower to centrally manage each account's S3 buckets.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10441" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use AWS Lake Formation to consolidate data from multiple accounts into a single account.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS Lake Formation</strong> is a service that makes it easy to set up a secure data lake in days. A data lake is a centralized, curated, and secured repository that stores all your data, both in its original form and prepared for analysis. A data lake enables you to break down data silos and combine different types of analytics to gain insights and guide better business decisions.</p>
<p>Amazon S3 forms the storage layer for Lake Formation. If you already use S3, you typically begin by registering existing S3 buckets that contain your data. Lake Formation creates new buckets for the data lake and import data into them. AWS always stores this data in your account, and only you have direct access to it.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/aws-lake-formation-glue-crawler.png" alt="" width="1000" height="540"></p>
<p>AWS Lake Formation is integrated with AWS Glue which you can use to create a data catalog that describes available datasets and their appropriate business applications.&nbsp;Lake Formation lets you define policies and control data access with simple “grant and revoke permissions to data” sets at granular levels.&nbsp;You can assign permissions to IAM users, roles, groups, and Active Directory users using federation. You specify permissions on catalog objects (like tables and columns) rather than on buckets and objects.</p>
<p>Thus, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Use AWS Lake Formation to consolidate data from multiple accounts into a single account.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Use AWS Kinesis Firehose to consolidate data from multiple accounts into a single account</strong></span> is incorrect. Setting up a Kinesis Firehose in each and every account to move data into a single location is costly and impractical. A better approach is to set up cross-account sharing which is free with AWS Lake Formation.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create a scheduled Lambda function for transferring data from multiple accounts to the S3 buckets of a central account</strong></span> is incorrect. This could be done by utilizing the AWS SDK, but implementation would be difficult and quite challenging to manage. Remember that the scenario explicitly mentioned that the solution must minimize management overhead.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Use AWS Control Tower to centrally manage each account’s S3 buckets&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect because the AWS Central Tower service is primarily used to manage and govern multiple AWS accounts and not just S3 buckets. Using the AWS Lake Formation service is a more suitable choice.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
