						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>59</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>59</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="197"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">A company is using AWS Fargate to run a batch job whenever an object is uploaded to an Amazon S3 bucket. The minimum ECS task count is initially set to 1 to save on costs and should only be increased based on new objects uploaded to the S3 bucket.</span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="446"><span class="fabric-text-color-mark" data-renderer-mark="true" data-text-custom-color="#ff5630">Which is the most suitable option to implement with the LEAST amount of effort?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="9929" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9929" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an alarm in CloudWatch to monitor S3 object-level operations recorded on CloudTrail. Set two alarm actions to update the ECS task count to scale-out/scale-in depending on the S3 event.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9929" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an alarm in Amazon CloudWatch to monitor S3 object-level operations that are recorded on CloudTrail. Create an Amazon EventBridge rule that triggers the ECS cluster when new CloudTrail events are detected.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9929" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Set up an Amazon EventBridge rule to detect S3 object PUT operations and set the target to the ECS cluster to run a new ECS task.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_9929" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> <span>Set up an Amazon EventBridge rule to detect S3 object PUT operations and set the target to a Lambda function that will run the <code>StartTask</code> API command.</span>												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon EventBridge (formerly called CloudWatch Events)</strong> is a serverless event bus that makes it easy to connect applications together. It uses data from your own applications, integrated software as a service (SaaS) applications, and AWS services. This simplifies the process of building event-driven architectures by decoupling event producers from event consumers. This allows producers and consumers to be scaled, updated, and deployed independently. Loose coupling improves developer agility in addition to application resiliency.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/eventbridge-diagram-sample.jpg" alt="" width="700" height="490"></p>
<p>You can use Amazon EventBridge&nbsp;to run Amazon ECS tasks when certain AWS events occur. You can set up an EventBridge rule that runs an Amazon ECS task whenever a file is uploaded to a certain Amazon S3 bucket using the Amazon S3 PUT operation.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is: <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>Set up an Amazon EventBridge rule to detect S3 object PUT operations and set the target to the ECS cluster to run a new ECS task.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up an Amazon EventBridge rule to detect S3 object PUT operations and set the target to a Lambda function that will run the <code>StartTask</code> API command&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect. Although this solution meets the requirement, creating your own Lambda function for this scenario is not really necessary. It is much simpler to control ECS tasks directly as targets for the CloudWatch Event rule. Take note that the scenario asks for a solution that is the easiest to implement.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up an alarm in Amazon CloudWatch to monitor S3 object-level operations that are recorded on CloudTrail. Create an Amazon EventBridge rule that triggers the ECS cluster when new CloudTrail events are detected&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect because using CloudTrail and CloudWatch Alarm creates an unnecessary complexity to what you want to achieve. Amazon EventBridge can directly target an ECS task on the Targets section when you create a new rule.</p>
<p>The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Set up an alarm in CloudWatch to monitor CloudTrail since this S3 object-level operations are recorded on CloudTrail. Set two alarm actions to update ECS task count to scale-out/scale-in depending on the S3 event</strong></span> is incorrect because you can’t directly set CloudWatch Alarms to update the ECS task count.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/events/CloudWatch-Events-tutorial-ECS.html " target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/events/CloudWatch-Events-tutorial-ECS.html </a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/events/Create-CloudWatch-Events-Rule.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonCloudWatch/latest/events/Create-CloudWatch-Events-Rule.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10072,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28901}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>60</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>60</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="206"><span data-renderer-mark="true">A company is in the process of migrating their applications to AWS. One of their systems requires a database that can scale globally and handle frequent schema changes. The application should not have any downtime or performance issues whenever there is a schema change in the database. It should also provide a low latency response to high-traffic queries. </span></p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="566"><span data-renderer-mark="true">Which is the most suitable database solution to use to achieve this requirement?</span></p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10072" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10072" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Amazon DynamoDB												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10072" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Redshift												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10072" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> An Amazon Aurora database with Read Replicas												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10072" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> An Amazon RDS instance in Multi-AZ Deployments configuration												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Before we proceed in answering this question, we must first be clear with the actual definition of a “<strong>schema</strong>“. Basically, the english definition of a schema is:&nbsp;<em>a representation of a plan or theory in the form of an outline or model</em>.</p>
<p>Just think of a schema as the “structure” or a “model” of your data in your database. Since the scenario requires that the schema, or the structure of your data, changes frequently, then you have to pick a database which provides a non-rigid and flexible way of adding or removing new types of data. This is a classic example of choosing between a relational database and non-relational (NoSQL) database.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-03-08_21-57-30-7860e883ac634eb2e771a5f4694cbafa.png" width="700" height="337"></p>
<p>A relational database is known for having a rigid schema, with a lot of constraints and limits as to which (and what type of ) data can be inserted or not. It is primarily used for scenarios where you have to support complex queries which fetch data across a number of tables. It is best for scenarios where you have complex table relationships but for use cases where you need to have a flexible schema, this is not a suitable database to use.</p>
<p>For NoSQL, it is not as rigid as a relational database because you can easily add or remove rows or elements in your table/collection entry. It also has a more flexible schema because&nbsp;it can store complex hierarchical data within a single item which, unlike a relational database, does not entail changing multiple related tables. Hence, the best answer to be used here is a NoSQL&nbsp;database, like DynamoDB. When your business requires a low-latency response to high-traffic queries, taking advantage of a NoSQL system generally makes technical and economic sense.</p>
<p>Amazon DynamoDB helps solve the problems that limit the relational system scalability by avoiding them.&nbsp;In DynamoDB, you design your schema specifically to make the most common and important queries as fast and as inexpensive as possible. Your data structures are tailored to the specific requirements of your business use cases.</p>
<p>Remember that a relational database system&nbsp;<strong>does not scale</strong>&nbsp;well for the following reasons:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– It normalizes data and stores it on multiple tables that require multiple queries to write to disk.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– It generally incurs the performance costs of an ACID-compliant transaction system.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– It uses expensive joins to reassemble required views of query results.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>For <strong><span style="color: #008000;">DynamoDB</span></strong>, it scales well due to these reasons:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Its<strong> schema flexibility</strong>&nbsp;lets DynamoDB store complex hierarchical data within a single item. DynamoDB is not a totally <em>schemaless</em> database since the very definition of a schema is just the model or structure of your data.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">– Composite key design lets it store related items close together on the same table.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>An Amazon RDS instance in Multi-AZ Deployments configuration</strong></span> and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>an Amazon Aurora database with Read Replicas</strong></span> are incorrect because both of them are a type of relational database.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Redshift</strong></span> is incorrect because it is primarily used for OLAP systems.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-general-nosql-design.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-general-nosql-design.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-relational-modeling.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/bp-relational-modeling.html</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/SQLtoNoSQL.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/amazondynamodb/latest/developerguide/SQLtoNoSQL.html</a></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Also check the <em><strong>AWS Certified Solutions Architect Official Study Guide: Associate Exam</strong></em> 1st Edition and turn to page 161 which talks about NoSQL Databases.</p>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10088,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28948}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>61</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>61</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A cryptocurrency trading platform is using an API built in AWS Lambda and API Gateway. Due to the recent news and rumors about the upcoming price surge of Bitcoin, Ethereum and other cryptocurrencies, it is expected that the trading platform would have a significant increase in site visitors and new users in the coming days ahead.</p>
<p>In this scenario, how can you protect the backend systems of the platform from traffic spikes?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10088" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10088" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Switch from using AWS Lambda and API Gateway to a more scalable and highly available architecture using EC2 instances, ELB, and Auto Scaling.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10088" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Enable throttling limits and result caching in API Gateway.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10088" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Use CloudFront in front of the API Gateway to act as a cache.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10088" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Move the Lambda function in a VPC.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon API Gateway</strong> provides throttling at multiple levels including global and by service call. Throttling limits can be set for standard rates and bursts. For example, API owners can set a rate limit of 1,000 requests per second for a specific method in their REST APIs, and also configure Amazon API Gateway to handle a burst of 2,000 requests per second for a few seconds. Amazon API Gateway tracks the number of requests per second. Any request over the limit will receive a 429 HTTP response. The client SDKs generated by Amazon API Gateway retry calls automatically when met with this response. Hence,&nbsp;<span style="color: #008000;"><strong>enabling throttling limits and result caching in API Gateway</strong></span> is the correct answer.</p>
<p>You can add caching to API calls by provisioning an Amazon API Gateway cache and specifying its size in gigabytes. The cache is provisioned for a specific stage of your APIs. This improves performance and reduces the traffic sent to your back end. Cache settings allow you to control the way the cache key is built and the time-to-live (TTL) of the data stored for each method. Amazon API Gateway also exposes management APIs that help you invalidate the cache for each stage.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/api-gw-settings.png" alt="" width="750-" height="462"></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Switch from using AWS Lambda and API Gateway to a more scalable and highly available architecture using EC2 instances, ELB, and Auto Scaling</strong></span> is incorrect since there is no need to transfer your applications to other services.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Using CloudFront in front of the API Gateway to act as a cache</strong></span> is incorrect because CloudFront only speeds up content delivery which provides a better latency experience for your users. It does not help much for the backend.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Moving the Lambda function in a VPC</strong></span> is incorrect because this answer is irrelevant to what is being asked. A VPC is your own virtual private cloud where you can launch AWS services.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference</strong>:</p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/faqs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/faqs/</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>62</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>62</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>A Forex trading platform, which frequently processes and stores global financial data every minute, is hosted in your on-premises data center and uses an Oracle database. Due to a recent cooling problem in their data center, the company urgently needs to migrate their infrastructure to AWS to improve the performance of their applications. As the Solutions Architect, you are responsible in ensuring that the database is properly migrated and should remain available in case of database server failure in the future.</p>
<p>Which of the following is the most suitable solution to meet the requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10081" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10081" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Oracle Real Application Clusters (RAC) in RDS.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10081" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Launch an Oracle database instance in RDS with Recovery Manager (RMAN) enabled.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10081" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Convert the database schema using the AWS Schema Conversion Tool and AWS Database Migration Service. Migrate the Oracle database to a non-cluster Amazon Aurora with a single instance.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10081" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an Oracle database in RDS with Multi-AZ deployments.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p>Amazon RDS Multi-AZ deployments provide enhanced availability and durability for Database (DB) Instances, making them a natural fit for production database workloads. When you provision a Multi-AZ DB Instance, Amazon RDS automatically creates a primary DB Instance and synchronously replicates the data to a standby instance in a different Availability Zone (AZ). Each AZ runs on its own physically distinct, independent infrastructure, and is engineered to be highly reliable.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/con-multi-AZ.png" alt="" width="484" height="344"></p>
<p>In case of an infrastructure failure, Amazon RDS performs an automatic failover to the standby (or to a read replica in the case of Amazon Aurora), so that you can resume database operations as soon as the failover is complete. Since the endpoint for your DB Instance remains the same after a failover, your application can resume database operation without the need for manual administrative intervention.</p>
<p>In this scenario, the best RDS configuration to use is an Oracle database in RDS with Multi-AZ deployments to ensure high availability even if the primary database instance goes down. Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>creating an Oracle database in RDS with Multi-AZ deployments</strong></span> is the correct answer.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Launching an Oracle database instance in RDS with Recovery Manager (RMAN) enabled</strong></span> and <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>launching an Oracle Real Application Clusters (RAC) in RDS</strong></span> are incorrect because Oracle RMAN and RAC are not supported in RDS.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Convert the database schema using the AWS Schema Conversion Tool and AWS Database Migration Service. Migrate the Oracle database to a non-cluster Amazon Aurora with a single instance</strong></span>&nbsp;is incorrect because although this solution is feasible, it takes time to migrate your Oracle database to&nbsp;Aurora, which is not acceptable. Based on this option, the&nbsp;Aurora database is only using a single instance with no Read Replica and is not configured as an Amazon Aurora DB cluster, which could have improved the availability of the database.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>References: </strong></p>
<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/details/multi-az/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Concepts.MultiAZ.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Concepts.MultiAZ.html</a></p>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10079,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28919}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>63</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>63</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p data-renderer-start-pos="165">A startup is using Amazon RDS to store data from a web application. Most of the time, the application has low user activity but it receives bursts of traffic within seconds whenever there is a new product announcement. The Solutions Architect needs to create a solution that will allow users around the globe to access the data using an API.</p>
<p data-renderer-start-pos="508">What should the Solutions Architect do meet the above requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10079" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10079" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use an Auto Scaling group of Amazon EC2 instances to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10079" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use Amazon Elastic Beanstalk with Auto Scaling to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds.
												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10079" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use the Amazon ECS cluster with Service Auto Scaling to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10079" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use AWS Lambda to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>AWS Lambda</strong> lets you run code without provisioning or managing servers. You pay only for the compute time you consume. With Lambda, you can run code for virtually any type of application or backend service – all with zero administration. Just upload your code, and Lambda takes care of everything required to run and scale your code with high availability. You can set up your code to automatically trigger from other AWS services or call it directly from any web or mobile app.</p>
<p>The first time you invoke your function, AWS Lambda creates an instance of the function and runs its handler method to process the event. When the function returns a response, it stays active and waits to process additional events. If you invoke the function again while the first event is being processed, Lambda initializes another instance, and the function processes the two events concurrently. As more events come in, Lambda routes them to available instances and creates new instances as needed. When the number of requests decreases, Lambda stops unused instances to free up the scaling capacity for other functions.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/features-scaling.png" alt="" width="700" height="389"></p>
<p>Your functions’&nbsp;<em>concurrency</em>&nbsp;is the number of instances that serve requests at a given time. For an initial burst of traffic, your functions’ cumulative concurrency in a Region can reach an initial level of between 500 and 3000, which varies per Region.</p>
<p>Based on the given scenario, you need to create a solution that will satisfy the two requirements. The first requirement is to create a solution that will allow the users to access the data using an API. To implement this solution, you can use Amazon API Gateway. The second requirement is to handle the burst of traffic within seconds. You should use AWS Lambda in this scenario because Lambda functions can absorb reasonable bursts of traffic for approximately 15-30 minutes.</p>
<p>Lambda can scale faster than the regular Auto Scaling feature of Amazon EC2, Amazon Elastic Beanstalk, or Amazon ECS. This is because AWS Lambda is more lightweight than other computing services. Under the hood, Lambda can run your code to thousands of available AWS-managed EC2 instances (that could already be running) within seconds to accommodate traffic. This is faster than the Auto Scaling process of launching new EC2 instances that could take a few minutes or so. An alternative is to overprovision your compute capacity but that will incur significant costs. The best option to implement given the requirements is a combination of AWS Lambda and Amazon API Gateway.</p>
<p>Hence, the correct answer is:<span style="color: #008000;"><strong> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use AWS Lambda to handle the bursts of traffic.</strong></span></p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use the Amazon ECS cluster with Service Auto Scaling to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect. AWS Lambda is a better option than Amazon ECS since it can handle a sudden burst of traffic within seconds and not minutes.</p>
<p>The option that says:<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong> Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use Amazon Elastic Beanstalk with Auto Scaling to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds&nbsp;</strong></span>is incorrect because just like the previous option, the use of Auto Scaling has a delay of a few minutes as it launches new EC2 instances that will be used by Amazon Elastic Beanstalk.</p>
<p>The option that says:<strong>&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;">Create an API using Amazon API Gateway and use an Auto Scaling group of Amazon EC2 instances to handle the bursts of traffic in seconds&nbsp;</span></strong>is incorrect because the processing time of Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling to provision new resources takes minutes. Take note that in the scenario, a burst of traffic within seconds is expected to happen.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/startups/from-0-to-100-k-in-seconds-instant-scale-with-aws-lambda/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/startups/from-0-to-100-k-in-seconds-instant-scale-with-aws-lambda/</a></p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/invocation-scaling.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/invocation-scaling.html</a></p>

						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>64</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>64</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design High-Performing Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An application hosted in EC2 consumes messages from an SQS queue and is integrated with SNS to send out an email to you once the process is complete. The Operations team received 5 orders but after a few hours, they saw 20 email notifications in their inbox.</p>
<p>Which of the following could be the possible culprit for this issue?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="2624" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_2624" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The web application is set to short polling so some messages are not being picked up.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_2624" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The web application is set for long polling so the messages are being sent twice.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_2624" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The web application does not have permission to consume messages in the SQS queue. 												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_2624" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> The web application is not deleting the messages in the SQS queue after it has processed them.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p style="text-align: left;">Always remember that the messages in the SQS queue will continue to exist even after the EC2 instance has processed it, until you delete that message. You have to ensure that you&nbsp;delete the message after processing to prevent the message from being received and processed again once the visibility timeout expires.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">There are three main parts in a distributed messaging system:</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">1. The components of your distributed system (EC2 instances)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">2. Your queue (distributed on Amazon SQS servers)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px; text-align: left;">3. Messages in the queue.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">You can set up a system which has several components that send messages to the queue and receive messages from the queue. The queue redundantly stores the messages across multiple Amazon SQS servers.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class="aligncenter" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/images/sqs-message-lifecycle-diagram.png"></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Refer to the third step of the SQS Message Lifecycle:</p>
<ol style="text-align: left;">
<li>Component 1 sends Message A to a queue, and the message is distributed across the Amazon SQS servers redundantly.</li>
<li>When Component 2 is ready to process a message, it consumes messages from the queue, and Message A is returned. While Message A is being processed, it remains in the queue and isn’t returned to subsequent receive requests for the duration of the visibility timeout.</li>
<li>Component 2 <strong>deletes</strong> Message A from the queue to prevent the message from being received and processed again once the visibility timeout expires.</li>
</ol>
<p style="text-align: left;">The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>The web application is set for long polling so the messages are being sent twice</strong></span> is incorrect because long polling helps reduce the cost of using SQS by eliminating the number of empty responses (when there are no messages available for a ReceiveMessage request) and false empty responses (when messages are available but aren’t included in a response). Messages being sent twice in&nbsp;an SQS queue configured with long polling is quite unlikely.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>The web application is set to short polling so some messages are not being picked up</strong></span> is incorrect since you are receiving emails from SNS where messages are certainly being processed. Following the scenario, messages not being picked up won’t result into 20 messages being sent to your inbox.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">The option that says: <span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>The web application does not have permission to consume messages in the SQS queue</strong></span> is incorrect because not having the correct permissions would have resulted in a different response. The scenario says that messages were properly processed but there were over 20 messages that were sent, hence, there is no problem with the accessing the queue.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>References:</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-message-lifecycle.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-message-lifecycle.html</a></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-basic-architecture.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-basic-architecture.html</a></p>

</p>
								</div>

											</li>

									<li class="wpProQuiz_listItem" style="" data-type="single" data-question-meta="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;single&quot;,&quot;question_pro_id&quot;:10119,&quot;question_post_id&quot;:28971}">
						<input class="ld_advanced_time_limit" type="hidden" name="ld_advanced_time_limit" id="ld_advanced_time_limit" value="0"><!--Added by webxity-->
						<div class="wpProQuiz_question_page" style="display:none;">
							Question <span>65</span> of <span>65</span>						</div>
						<h5 style="display: inline-block;" class="wpProQuiz_header">
							<span>65</span>. Question
						</h5>

						
													<div style="font-weight: bold; padding-top: 5px;">
								Category: <span>CSAA – Design Resilient Architectures</span>							</div>
												<div class="wpProQuiz_question" style="margin: 10px 0px 0px 0px;">
							<div class="wpProQuiz_question_text">
								<p>An online shopping platform is hosted on an Auto Scaling group of Spot EC2 instances and uses Amazon Aurora PostgreSQL as its database. There is a requirement to optimize your database workloads in your cluster where you have to direct the production traffic to your high-capacity instances and point the reporting queries sent by your internal staff to the low-capacity instances.</p>
<p>Which is the most suitable configuration for your application as well as your Aurora database cluster to achieve this requirement?</p>
							</div>
							<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>

														

							 
							<ul class="wpProQuiz_questionList" data-question_id="10119" data-type="single">
								
										
										
										
										
										
										
										
																	<li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="3">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">1. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10119" value="4" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Do nothing since by default, Aurora will automatically direct the production traffic to your high-capacity instances and the reporting queries to your low-capacity instances.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem wpProQuiz_answerCorrectIncomplete" data-pos="2">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">2. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10119" value="3" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Create a custom endpoint in Aurora based on the specified criteria for the production traffic and another custom endpoint to handle the reporting queries.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="1">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">3. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10119" value="2" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> In your application, use the instance endpoint of your Aurora database to handle the incoming production traffic and use the cluster endpoint to handle reporting queries.												</label>


																																</li><li class="wpProQuiz_questionListItem" data-pos="0">


																																																										<span style="display:none;">4. </span>
												<label>
													<input class="wpProQuiz_questionInput bbstyled" type="radio" name="question_45_10119" value="1" disabled="disabled"><span class="input-style"></span> Configure your application to use the reader endpoint for both production traffic and reporting queries, which will enable your Aurora database to automatically perform load-balancing among all the Aurora Replicas.												</label>


																																</li></ul>
						</div>
												<p class="wpProQuiz_clear" style="clear:both;"></p>
													<div class="wpProQuiz_response" style="">
								<div style="display: none;" class="wpProQuiz_correct">
																			<span>Correct</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage">
									</p>
								</div>
								<div style="" class="wpProQuiz_incorrect">
																			<span>
									Incorrect								</span>
																		<p class="wpProQuiz_AnswerMessage"><p><strong>Amazon Aurora</strong> typically involves a cluster of DB instances instead of a single instance. Each connection is handled by a specific DB instance. When you connect to an Aurora cluster, the host name and port that you specify point to an intermediate handler called an&nbsp;<em>endpoint</em>. Aurora uses the endpoint mechanism to abstract these connections. Thus, you don’t have to hardcode all the hostnames or write your own logic for load-balancing and rerouting connections when some DB instances aren’t available.</p>
<p>For certain Aurora tasks, different instances or groups of instances perform different roles. For example, the primary instance handles all data definition language (DDL) and data manipulation language (DML) statements. Up to 15 Aurora Replicas handle read-only query traffic.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://media.tutorialsdojo.com/2019-04-03_00-40-18-850e58ca7802358579be53729bfc0cbb.gif" alt="" width="880" height="423"></p>
<p>Using endpoints, you can map each connection to the appropriate instance or group of instances based on your use case. For example, to perform DDL statements you can connect to whichever instance is the primary instance. To perform queries, you can connect to the reader endpoint, with Aurora automatically performing load-balancing among all the Aurora Replicas. For clusters with DB instances of different capacities or configurations, you can connect to custom endpoints associated with different subsets of DB instances. For diagnosis or tuning, you can connect to a specific instance endpoint to examine details about a specific DB instance.</p>
<p>The custom endpoint provides load-balanced database connections based on criteria other than the read-only or read-write capability of the DB instances. For example, you might define a custom endpoint to connect to instances that use a particular AWS instance class or a particular DB parameter group. Then you might tell particular groups of users about this custom endpoint. For example, you might direct internal users to low-capacity instances for report generation or ad hoc (one-time) querying, and direct production traffic to high-capacity instances. Hence, <span style="color: #008000;"><strong>creating a custom endpoint in Aurora based on the specified criteria for the production traffic and another custom endpoint to handle the reporting queries</strong></span> is the correct answer.</p>
<p><span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Configuring your application to use the reader endpoint for both production traffic and reporting queries, which will enable your Aurora database to automatically perform load-balancing among all the Aurora Replicas</strong></span> is incorrect. Although it is true that a reader endpoint enables your Aurora database to automatically perform load-balancing among all the Aurora Replicas, it is quite limited to doing read operations only. You still need to use a custom endpoint to load-balance the database connections based on the specified criteria.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>In your application, use the instance endpoint of your Aurora database to handle the incoming production traffic and use the cluster endpoint to handle reporting queries</strong></span> is incorrect because&nbsp;a cluster endpoint (also known as a writer endpoint) for an Aurora DB cluster simply connects to the current primary DB instance for that DB cluster. This endpoint can perform write operations in the database such as DDL statements, which is perfect for handling production traffic but not suitable for handling queries for reporting since there will be no write database operations that will be sent. Moreover, the endpoint does not point to lower-capacity or high-capacity instances as per the requirement. A better solution for this is to use a custom endpoint.</p>
<p>The option that says:&nbsp;<span style="color: #ff6600;"><strong>Do nothing since by default, Aurora will automatically direct the production traffic to your high-capacity instances and the reporting queries to your low-capacity instances</strong></span> is incorrect because Aurora does not do this by default. You have to create custom endpoints in order to accomplish this requirement.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Reference</strong>:</p>
<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/Aurora.Overview.Endpoints.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/AuroraUserGuide/Aurora.Overview.Endpoints.html</a></p>
